The Proof for Allah's Pre-Eternity (Qidam)
Sanusi proves Allah's pre-eternity by showing the impossibility of origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that Allah must be pre-eternal (qadim) and cannot be originated (hadith), based on the impossibility of infinite regress and circularity.

Core Idea
Allah must be pre-eternal; assuming otherwise leads to an absurd infinite chain.

This passage presents a formal kalam argument for Allah's attribute of qidam (pre-eternity). The argument uses the law of excluded middle and a reductio ad absurdum: if Allah were originated, He would need an originator, leading to an infinite regress or circularity, both impossible. Therefore, the opposite—pre-eternity—must be true. The student should follow each step carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the structure
Read the Arabic source and its translation. Notice that the argument is a conditional proof: if not pre-eternal, then originated; if originated, then need originator; then leads to impossible consequences.
2
Understand the key concepts
Focus on the definitions of pre-eternity (qidam) and origination (huduth), and the two impossible outcomes: infinite regress (tasalsul) and circularity (dawr).
Tasalsul is an unending chain of causes; dawr is a cycle where A depends on B and B depends on A.
3
Trace the logical chain and confirm the conclusion
Follow the implication chain: ¬qidam → huduth → need for originator → either tasalsul or dawr → impossible → so huduth is impossible → so qidam is necessary.
The conclusion is the opposite of the original assumption, established by impossibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على وجوب قدمه تعالى: أنه لو لم يكن قديماً لكان حادثا ، إذ لا واسطة بين القدم والحدوث ، ولا يجوز أن يكونَ لا قديما ولا حادثا ؛ لأنَّ ذلك ارتفاع النقيضين؛ وهو مُحال كاجتماعهما ، ولو كانَ حادثاً لافتقر إلى مُحدِثٍ يحدِثُه، ولو افتقر إلى مُحدث لافتقرَ مُحدِثُه إلى مُحدِثٍ ؛ لأنَّ محدثه مثله ،وهكذا، فإن استمر الأمر إلى ما لا نهاية لزِمَ التّسلسل، وإنْ رجع إلى الأول لزِمَ الدَّورُ ، وكل منهما مُحالٌ ، فما أدى إليهما ـ وهو افتقاره إلى محدث ـ محالٌ ؛ فما أدى إليه - وهو كونه سبحانه مُحدثًا - مُحَالٌ ، فثبتَ نَقيضُه؛ وهو كونه تعالى قديما : ، وهو المطلوب.
The proof for the necessity of His pre-eternity, Exalted is He: that if He were not pre-eternal, He would be originated, since there is no middle between pre-eternity and origination. And it is not permissible that He be neither pre-eternal nor originated, because that would be the removal of two contradictories, which is impossible just as their conjunction is impossible. And if He were originated, He would need an originator to originate Him. And if He needed an originator, then His originator would need an originator, because His originator is like Him, and so on. If the matter continues to infinity, then infinite regress (tasalsul) follows. And if it goes back to the first, then circularity (dawr) follows. And both are impossible. Therefore, what leads to them – namely, His need for an originator – is impossible. And what leads to that – namely, His being originated, glory be to Him – is impossible. So its opposite is established: that He, Exalted is He, is pre-eternal. And that is the desired conclusion.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage provides a formal proof for Allah's attribute of qidam (pre-eternity). The argument is based on the law of excluded middle: either God is pre-eternal (qadim) or originated (hadith). Assuming originated leads to the need for an originator, which then would itself need an originator, leading either to an infinite regress (tasalsul) or a circular argument (dawr), both of which are impossible. Therefore, the assumption that God is originated is impossible, so He must be pre-eternal.

Key Terms

الحدوث
النقيضين
التسلسل
الدور
المحدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is circular because it assumes what it tries to prove.
Correction: The argument is not circular; it is a reductio ad absurdum. It assumes the opposite (that Allah is originated) and derives an impossibility, thereby proving the original claim by contradiction.

Checkpoint
What does the proof conclude if we assume God is originated?
A) That God does not exist
B) That an infinite regress or circularity results, which is impossible
C) That God is eternal
D) That the argument is invalid

Key Takeaway
Allah's pre-eternity is rationally necessary because assuming origination leads to an impossible infinite regress or circularity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The argument shows that an infinite chain of causes is impossible. Consider your own daily dependencies – on food, air, people. At the end of every chain, you find a single pre-eternal being. How does knowing that your existence is ultimately anchored in Allah change the way you face your anxieties today? What one worry will you hand over to Him right now?
?
If Allah were not pre-eternal, He would need an originator. That means everything you rely on for security – your health, wealth, relationships – is only stable because its source is without beginning. Are you living as if your ultimate security comes from originated things that will perish? What is one concrete step you will take today to shift your trust from the originated to the Pre-Eternal?
?
Impossibility of circularity means that your dependence cannot loop back to yourself. You cannot be your own originator. In what areas of your life are you trying to be self-sufficient, as if you are the cause of your own success or righteousness? How will you acknowledge your need for the Pre-Eternal in your next action?

Al-Qidam: Definition and Proof of Divine Past Eternity
Defines qidam as un-precededness and proves by contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-qidam (past eternity) and the rational proof that establishes it for Allah.

Core Idea
Allah's existence is un-preceded by non-existence — otherwise, an infinite regress would follow.

This lesson introduces one of the essential divine attributes: qidam, or past eternity. Sanusi defines it precisely and then offers a powerful proof by contradiction. As you will see, the proof shows that denying qidam leads to an impossible chain of causes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the compact style: definition followed immediately by a conditional proof.
2
Understand the definition
Identify the exact phrasing of the definition: 'qidam is existence not preceded by non-existence'. Note that 'qadim' means 'that which has no beginning'.
This is the precise theological meaning, not merely 'old'.
3
Follow the proof's logic
The proof is a conditional argument: if qadim had a beginning, it would need a creator; that creator would also need a creator, and so on, due to similarity. This leads to infinite regress or circularity.
Both regress and circularity are deemed impossible by rational necessity.
4
Reflect on the impossibility
Why are infinite regress and circularity impossible? Reflect on the fact that an infinite chain of dependent beings cannot be actual, and circularity would imply self-causation. The impossibility of the consequence proves the impossibility of the antecedent.
This establishes qidam as necessary for Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات
القدم، أي: أن يكون وجوده غير مسبوق بعدم؛ إذ القديم ما لا أوَّلَ له، وإلا لزِمَ افتقاره تعالى إلى مُحدث ثم مُحدِثُه ومحدث محدثه، وهلم جرا؛ لانعقاد المُماثلة بين الكلِّ، وذلك مُفضِ إلى التّسلسل أو الدور، وكلاهما محال، فملزومها كذلك.
Section on Divine Matters. Al-Qidam (past eternity): that His existence be not preceded by non-existence; for the eternal (al-qadim) is that which has no beginning. Otherwise, His, Exalted, need of a creator would follow, then of its creator and the creator of its creator, and so on, due to the similarity between all, and that leads to infinite regress (tasalsul) or circularity (dawr), both of which are impossible, so their implication is likewise [impossible].
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage provides the definition and proof of al-qidam (past eternity) as a divine attribute. It begins by stating the section: 'Section on Divine Matters.' Then it defines qidam as existence not preceded by non-existence; the eternal is that which has no beginning. The proof is an argument by contradiction: if Allah had a beginning, He would need a creator. That creator would then need another creator, and so on, because all originated beings are similar in requiring a cause. This leads to either infinite regress (tasalsul) or circularity (dawr), both of which are impossible. Therefore, the assumption of a beginning is also impossible, thus establishing the necessity of qidam for Allah.

Key Terms
قدم
تسلسل
دور
مماثلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'qadim' simply means 'old' or 'ancient' in time.
Correction: In aqeedah, qadim means 'un-preceded by non-existence' — it is a logical priority, not temporal age.

Checkpoint
What does the proof of qidam aim to refute?
A) That Allah has no beginning.
B) That Allah has a beginning.
C) That Allah is eternal in the future.
D) That Allah is self-sufficient.

Key Takeaway
Qidam is an essential divine attribute: Allah's existence is not preceded by non-existence, proven by the impossibility of infinite regress or circularity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah alone is qadim—un-preceded by non-existence—then everything else, including your own existence, is entirely dependent on Him. Do you truly live as if only Allah is self-sufficient, or do you sometimes treat people, possessions, or plans as if they were eternally reliable? What would change today if you fully internalized that only Allah has no beginning?
?
The proof shows that imagining a beginning for Allah leads to an absurd infinite regress or circular reasoning. Have you ever justified disobedience or delayed repentance by thinking 'there's always time'—essentially assuming that your existence is self-evident and unaccountable? How does the urgency of Allah's absolute eternity confront that assumption right now?
?
You have just learned that 'al-qadim' means having no beginning at all—not merely being old. Does your heart attribute this kind of absolute pre-eternity to anything other than Allah—such as your own habits, desires, or pride? Name one thing you have treated as if it were 'always there' and commit to reframing it as originated and dependent on Allah alone.

Proof of God's Unlikeness to Creation (Mukhalafah)
Al-Sanusi provides the conditional proof that God must be unlike accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the conditional proof that God must be unlike originated things (mukhalafah) and how it depends on the proof of His eternity (qidam).

Core Idea
God's unlikeness to creation is proven by a simple conditional argument.

How do we know that God is not like anything in creation? Al-Sanusi presents a tightly structured proof that begins with a conditional: if God were similar to originated things, He would be originated. Since He is eternal (qidam), He cannot be similar, so He must be unlike them. In this lesson, we will unpack the logic of this argument and see how it connects to the earlier proof of God's eternity.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof statement
Read the Arabic and translation of the conditional proof carefully. Notice the structure: a conditional chain leading to a conclusion.
The proof is in two parts: the initial matn line and the commentary's formal argument.
2
Identify the conditional chain
Break down the proof into its premises: if not mukhalaf → mumathala, and if mumathala → hadith. Then see how the negation of hadith (by qidam) leads to the conclusion of mukhalafah.
3
Understand the reliance on qidam
The proof requires that God is not originated. This was already established by the proof of qidam (eternity). Al-Sanusi points this out explicitly.
This shows that attributes are interconnected; the proof of one attribute often relies on another.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنه لما ينال العدم مخالف برهان هذا القدم. وأما الدليل على وجوب مخالفته سبحانه للحوادث ، فتقريره أنه لو لم يكن مخالفًا للحوادث لكان مماثلاً لها ، ولو كان مماثلاً لها لكان حادثاً، لكنه سبحانه ليس بحادث، فلا يكون مماثلا للحوادث. أما الدليل على أنه سبحانه ليس بحادث فهو دليل القدم الذي قدمناه آنفًا ، وهذا هو في هذا الدليل، ولذلك قال المصنف : «برهان هذا القدم» وإذا استحال كونه مماثلًا للحوادث ثبت كونه مخالفًا لها ، وهو المطلوب. قول المصنف : (وأنه لما ينال العدم مخالف) الضمير المنصوب محلا بـ«أن عائد على الله تعالى، وخبر «أن» هو قوله : (مخالف) و«اللام» في قوله: (لما ينال العدم) متعلق بمخالف و ما موصولة وجملة: ينال العدم لا محل لها صلة ، والعائد محذوف ، والتقدير : وأنه تعالى مخالف للذي يناله العدم، ومعنى يناله العدم» يلحقه العدم ويطرأ عليه ، والذي يلحقه العدم ويطرأ عليه هو الحادث، فكأنه قال: وأنه مخالف للحوادث ، وأنت خبير بأن: «أن المفتوحة الهمزة تسبك ما بعدها بمصدر يكون معطوفا على الوجود، وعلى هذا ينحل هذا الكلام إلى قولنا وواجب له مخالفته للحوادث ، وهذه هي الصفة الثالثة من السلبية . محي.
And that He is unlike that which is reached by non-existence — the proof of this is [the proof of] eternity (qidam). As for the proof of the necessity of His being unlike created things, its formulation is: if He were not unlike created things, He would be similar to them, and if He were similar to them, He would be originated (hadith), but He is not originated, so He is not similar to created things. As for the proof that He is not originated, it is the proof of eternity which we presented earlier, and this is the crux of this proof, therefore the author said: 'the proof of this is [the proof of] eternity.' And if His being similar to created things is impossible, His being unlike them is established, and that is what is sought. The statement of the author: 'And that He is unlike that which is reached by non-existence' — the pronoun in the accusative place connected to 'an' refers to God Almighty, and the predicate of 'an' is His statement 'unlike', and the lam in His statement 'for that which is reached by non-existence' is attached to 'unlike', and 'ma' is a relative pronoun, and the sentence 'it is reached by non-existence' has no place as a relative clause, and the relative pronoun is omitted. The estimation is: 'and that He, exalted, is unlike that which is reached by non-existence.' The meaning of 'reached by non-existence' is that non-existence attaches to it and befalls it, and that which non-existence attaches to and befalls is the originated thing. So it is as if He said: 'and that He is unlike originated things.' And you know that the 'anna' with open hamza (an) creates a verbal noun that is coordinated with existence. According to this, this statement resolves into our saying: 'and it is necessary for Him to be unlike originated things,' and this is the third of the negative attributes. Muhyi.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage provides the proof (dalil) for the necessity of the attribute of mukhalafah. It begins by referencing the line from the matn: 'And that He is unlike that which is reached by non-existence – the proof of this is [the proof of] eternity.' This line is a prelude. Then the formal proof is given: it is a conditional argument (qiyas shurti). The proof states: If God were not unlike created things, He would be similar to them. And if He were similar to them, He would be originated (hadith). But God is not originated (as proven by the proof of qidam). Therefore, it is impossible for Him to be similar to created things, and consequently He must be unlike them. The proof relies on the earlier established proof of God's eternity (qidam). The author (al-Sanusi) refers to this by saying 'the proof of this is [the proof of] eternity.' After presenting the proof, the passage then gives a grammatical and logical analysis of the initial verse from the matn ('And that He is unlike that which is reached by non-existence'). The commentator explains the parsing: the pronoun refers to God, 'ma' is a relative noun meaning 'that which', and 'yanaluhu al-`adam' (non-existence reaches it) describes the originated thing. So the phrase essentially means 'And that He is unlike originated things.' The commentator also notes that the 'an' with fatha creates a verbal noun, making the phrase coordinate with 'existence' in the earlier enumeration of necessary attributes. Thus, this is the third of the negative attributes.

Key Terms
مخالفة للحوادث
مماثلة
حدوث
قدم
برهان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof of mukhalafah is circular because it uses the proof of qidam which itself depends on mukhalafah.
Correction: The proof of qidam was established independently (based on the impossibility of a regress or other arguments). Mukhalafah is derived from qidam, not the other way around. The proof is linear: first prove qidam, then use it to prove mukhalafah.

Checkpoint

B) God is unlike created things
C) God has no attributes
D) God is corporeal

Key Takeaway
God's unlikeness to creation is proven logically from His eternity: if He were like originated things, He would be originated, but He is not, so He must be unlike them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

This proof shows that any such imagination would make God like originated things, and thus not God. Examine your heart: have you unknowingly shaped God in the image of something you know? What steps will you take today to purify your conception of God based on this proof?

If God were like created things, He would be subject to change and decay. How does the certainty that God is unlike anything else affect your trust in Him? Does your daily reliance on Him reflect that He alone is eternal and unchanging, or do you still put your hope in temporary things? Commit to one concrete action this week that demonstrates your trust in the Uncreated.
?
The proof of mukhalafah depends entirely on God's eternity. Have you truly internalized that God has no beginning and no end? How would your life change if you lived with constant awareness that you are standing before the Eternal One, who is utterly unlike anything you experience? Describe one change you will make starting today.

The Proof for the Oneness of Allah
Sanusi presents a logical proof by contradiction for Allah's oneness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof (dalīl) that Allah is one in essence and attributes, based on a reductio ad absurdum argument that any multiplicity of gods leads to an impossibility.

Core Idea
The oneness of Allah is proven by showing that assuming multiple gods leads to impossible consequences.

Sanusi presents a powerful logical proof for tawḥīd, grounded in the observable existence of the world. By assuming the opposite — that there are multiple gods — he demonstrates that each possible scenario results in an absurdity, thereby confirming that Allah is one without parallel. The proof is structured as a series of cases, each of which is shown to be impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof statement
Start by reading the opening lines of the passage where Sanusi states the conclusion: if multiplicity were true, the world would not exist. Since the world does exist, multiplicity is false and oneness is true.
Notice that the proof is a conditional argument: if P (multiplicity), then Q (no world); not Q (world exists), therefore not P.
2
Identify the key assumption
The proof assumes two gods exist. Then it explores all possibilities: they agree or disagree. Under agreement, there are three subcases; under disagreement, three more. Each subcase is examined for impossibility.
3
Trace the agreement cases
Follow the three cases under agreement: creating together (two perfect causes on one effect), sequential creation (repetition of the already existent), and separate creation (each incapable of the other's action). Each is deemed impossible.
The passage provides explicit reasoning for why each is impossible.
4
Examine the disagreement cases
Under disagreement, three possibilities: each will is executed (contradiction), one will is executed (implies the other is not omnipotent), or neither will is executed (both are weak). The passage is cut off at the second case, but the pattern is clear.
Even with the incomplete text, we can see that all options lead to absurdity, proving the initial assumption of multiplicity is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الدليل على أنه سبحانه واحد في ذاته وفي صفاته بمعنى عدم النظير فيهما فَمُلَخصه أن نقول: لو لم يكن واحدًا لكان متعددا ، ولو كان متعددا.. لما وجد شيء من هذا العالم، لكن عدم وجود شيء من العالم باطل، فما أدى إليه - وهو التَّعدُّد - باطل، وإذا بطَلَ التَّعدد ثبت وهو أنه واحدٌ ، وهو المطلوب. فأما بطلان عدم وجود شيء من هذا العالم فثابت بالمشاهدة. وأمَّا التَّلازم بين التعدّد وعدم وجود شيء من العالم أنه إذا تعدد بأن كان في العالم إلهان فإما أن يتفقا ، وإما أن يختلفا، فإن اتفقا ، فإما أن يتفقا على الاشتراك في إيجاد كل شيء، وإما أن يتفقا على انفراد كل واحد منهما بشيء، فإن اتفقا على إيجاد كل شيء فإما أن يتفقا على أن يوجداه معا، وإما أن يتفقا على أن يوجده أحدهما ثم يوجده الآخر بعده، فإن اتفقا على أن يوجداه معا، والمفروض أنَّ كل واحد منهما تام القدرة كان في إيجادهما إياه معا اجتماع مؤثرين كل واحد منهما قادر تام القدرة على أثر واحد وهو لا يجوز، وإن اتفقا على أن يوجد أحدهما الشيء ثم يوجده الآخر كان في إيجاد الثاني إياه تحصيل الحاصل وهو محال، وإن اتفقا على أن يوجد أحدهما شيئا ويوجد الآخر شيئا آخر لزم أن يكون كل واحد منهما عاجزا عن إيجاد ما أوجده الآخر فهما جميعا على هذا الفرض عاجزان، وإن اختلفا فإما أن ينفذ مراد أحدهما دون الآخر وإما أن ينفذ مراد كل منهما وإما ألا ينفذ مراد واحد منهما، فإن نفذ مراد كل منهما لزم اجتماع النقيضين وهو محال، وإن نفذ مراد أحدهما دون الآخر لزم=
As for the proof that He, glorified is He, is one in His essence and His attributes in the sense of having no parallel in them, its summary is that we say: If He were not one, He would be multiple; and if He were multiple, then nothing of this world would exist. But the non-existence of something of this world is false, so what leads to it—namely multiplicity—is false. And if multiplicity is false, then it is established that He is one, which is the desired conclusion. As for the falsehood of the non-existence of something of this world, it is established by observation. As for the necessary connection between multiplicity and the non-existence of something of this world: that if there is multiplicity, meaning there are two gods in the world, then either they agree or they disagree. If they agree, then either they agree on sharing the bringing into existence of every thing, or they agree on each one being alone with a thing. If they agree on bringing everything into existence, then either they agree that they bring it into existence together, or they agree that one brings it into existence then the other brings it into existence afterwards. If they agree that they bring it into existence together, and the assumption is that each of them is perfect in power, then in their bringing it into existence together there is a conjunction of two effective agents each of whom is capable, perfect in power, upon a single effect, which is not permissible. And if they agree that one brings the thing into existence and then the other brings it into existence, then in the second bringing it into existence there is a repetition of what is already realized (taḥṣīl al-ḥāṣil), which is impossible. And if they agree that one brings one thing into existence and the other brings another thing into existence, then it follows that each of them is incapable of bringing into existence what the other brought into existence, so both, on this assumption, are incapable. And if they disagree, then either the will of one is executed without the other, or the will of each is executed, or the will of neither is executed. If the will of each is executed, then the conjunction of two contradictories (ijtimā‘ al-naqīḍayn) follows, which is impossible. And if the will of one is executed without the other, then it follows that...
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage presents a logical proof (dalīl) for the oneness of Allah in essence and attributes, meaning the negation of any parallel. The proof is an argument by contradiction: assume multiplicity, then derive an impossibility, so multiplicity is false, and oneness is true. The author states the conclusion first, then explains the steps. The key is that if there were two gods, either they agree or disagree, and both scenarios lead to absurdities. The cases: (1) agreeing to create together leads to two perfect causes on one effect, impossible; (2) one creates then the other creates a second time leads to repetition of the already existent; (3) each creates different things implies inability to create what the other does; (4) if they disagree and each will is executed, contradiction arises; (5) if only one will is executed, the other is not omnipotent. The proof is cut off at the last case, but the conclusion is already stated: multiplicity is false, so oneness is true. The contrast with observed existence is used to show that the world does exist, so multiplicity cannot be the case.

الدليل (al-dālīl)
التعدد (al-ta‘addud)
الوحدانية (al-waḥdāniyya)
اجتماع النقيضين (ijtimā‘ al-naqīḍayn)
تحصيل الحاصل (taḥṣīl al-ḥāṣil)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof for oneness only applies to Allah's essence, not His attributes.
Correction: The passage explicitly states 'one in His essence and His attributes in the sense of having no parallel in them,' confirming that the proof covers both.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The existence of the world logically necessitates a single, unique Creator, as any multiplicity leads to an absurdity.

This proof forces you to accept that the entire universe's existence hinges on Allah's absolute oneness. When you feel anxious or desperate, do you act as if there is another power that can help you? What specific thought or action can you replace that with, starting now?

Proof of Oneness by Contradiction of Multiplicity
Sanusi proves God's oneness via reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof for God's oneness based on the impossibility of multiple creators, as argued by Sanusi.

Core Idea
If there were two gods, the world could not exist — proving oneness is necessary.

This passage presents a classic kalam argument for tawḥīd — the proof by contradiction of multiplicity. The argument assumes the existence of the world as observed, and shows that any scenario with multiple gods leads to logical absurdities. By eliminating all possibilities, the oneness of the Creator is established.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage Carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the overall flow of the argument. Do not get bogged down in details yet.
Notice the repeated structure: 'if they agree... if they differ...'
2
Trace the Logical Branches
The argument examines two main scenarios: the gods agree or differ. Within agreement, there are sub-branches. Identify the impossibility in each branch (e.g., two effectors on one effect, obtaining the already obtained, mutual incapacity).
Use the guided breakdown below if you need help following the steps.
3
Synthesize the Conclusion
After seeing that all scenarios lead to impossibility, conclude that the assumption of multiplicity is false. Therefore, God is one in essence and attributes.
The proof relies on the observed existence of the world — that is the only empirical premise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الدليل على أنه سبحانه واحد في ذاته وفي صفاته بمعنى عدم النظير فيهما فَمُلَخصه أن نقول: نقيضه - فدليله: لو لم يكن واحدًا لكان متعددا ، ولو كان متعددا.. لما وجد شيء من هذا العالم، لكن عدم وجود شيء من العالم باطل، فما أدى إليه - وهو التَّعدُّد - باطل، وإذا بطَلَ التَّعدد ثبت وهو أنه واحدٌ ، وهو المطلوب. فأما بطلان عدم وجود شيء من هذا العالم فثابت بالمشاهدة. وأمَّا التَّلازم بين التعدّد وعدم وجود شيء من العالم أنه إذا تعدد ـ بأن كان في العالم إلهان - فإما أنْ يتفقا ، وإما أنْ يختلفا، فإن اتفقا ، فإما أن يتفقا على الاشتراك في إيجاد كلَّ شيء، وإما أن يتفقا على انفراد كلّ واحدٍ منهما بشيء، فإن اتفقا على إيجاد كل شيء، فإما أن يتفقا على أن يوجداه معا، وإما أن يتفقا على أن يوجده أحدهما ثم يوجده ثم يوجده الآخر بعده، فإن اتفقا على أن يوجداه معا، والمفروض أنَّ كل واحدٍ منهما تام القدرة ، كان في إيجادهما إياه معا اجتماع مؤثرين كلُّ واحدٍ منهما قادر تام القدرة على أثر واحدٍ وهو لا يجوز، وإن اتفقا على أن يوجد أحدهما الشيء ثم يوجده الآخر، كان في إيجاد الثاني إيَّاه تحصيل الحاصل وهو مُحال، وإن اتفقا على أن أحدهما شيئا ويوجد الآخر شيئا آخر لزم أن يكون كل واحد منهما عاجزا عن إيجاد ما أوجده الآخر، فهما جميعاً - على هذا الفرض - عاجزان ، وإن اختلفا ؛ فإما أن ينفذ مراد أحدهما دون الآخر ، وإما أن ينفذ مراد كل منهما ، وإما ألا ينفذ مراد واحد منهما، فإن نفذ مراد كل منهما لزم اجتماع النقيضين وهو محال ، وإن نفذ مراد أحدهما دون الآخر لزم أن يكون من لم ينفذ مراده عاجزا ، ولزم أن يكون الآخر أيضا عاجزا، إذ الفرض أنهما متساويان في القدرة والعلم وغيرهما من الصفات، وإن لم ينفذ مراد واحد منهما، لزم أن يكون كل واحد منهما عاجزا ، وكل هذه اللوازم محال ، فما أدى إليها ـ وهو التَّعدُّد ـ محالٌ ، فثبت نقيضه ـ وهو عدم التعدد ـ وأن الخالق المدبر لهذا الكون واحد في ذاته وفي صفاته ، وهو المطلوب.
As for the proof that He, exalted, is one in His essence and in His attributes, meaning lack of peer in them, its summary is that we say: its opposite - so its proof: if He were not one, He would be multiple, and if He were multiple... then nothing of this world would exist. But the non-existence of something from the world is false by observation. So what leads to it - multiplicity - is false. And when multiplicity is false, its opposite is established, namely that He is one. And that is the desired. As for the falsity of non-existence of anything from the world, it is established by observation. And as for the necessary connection between multiplicity and non-existence of anything from the world: if there is multiplicity - that there are in the world two gods - then either they agree or they differ. If they agree, then either they agree to share in bringing every thing into existence, or they agree on each one's having exclusive production of something. If they agree on bringing every thing into existence, then either they agree to bring it into existence together, or they agree that one brings it into existence then the other brings it into existence afterwards. If they agree to bring it into existence together, and it is assumed that each of them is perfect in power, then their bringing it into existence together would be the convergence of two effectors, each of them powerful, perfect in power, on one effect, which is not permissible. If they agree that one brings the thing into existence then the other brings it, then the second's bringing it into existence would be the obtaining of the already obtained, which is impossible. If they agree that one [produces] one thing and the other produces another thing, then each of them would be incapable of producing what the other produced, so both - in this supposition - are incapable. And if they differ: then either the will of one alone is executed, or the will of each is executed, or neither's will is executed. If the will of each is executed, that necessitates the composition of two opposites, which is impossible. If the will of one alone is executed, then the one whose will is not executed would be incapable, and the other would also be incapable, since it is assumed they are equal in power, knowledge, and other attributes. If neither's will is executed, then each would be incapable. And all these consequences are impossible. So what leads to them - multiplicity - is impossible. Therefore its opposite - the absence of multiplicity - is established, and that the Creator, the Disposer of this universe, is one in His essence and His attributes. And that is the desired.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage presents a logical proof for God's oneness by reductio ad absurdum. It begins by stating the desired conclusion: that God is one in essence and attributes with no peer. The proof proceeds by assuming the opposite (multiplicity) and showing it leads to contradiction.

Structure:
- Assume multiplicity (two gods).
- Then either they agree or differ.
- If they agree, further subdivisions lead to impossibility (e.g., two agents on one effect is impossible; producing what already exists is impossible; exclusive domains imply mutual incapacity).
- If they differ, either both wills are executed (leading to opposites together), one executed (the other incapable, and since equal, both incapable), or neither executed (both incapable).
- All these scenarios are impossible; hence, the assumption of multiplicity is false; therefore, God is one.

This classic argument (burhān al-tamānu' in its condensed form) relies on the observed existence of the world and the logical consequences of polytheism.

Key Terms
تعدد
إلهان
اجتماع المؤثرين
تحصيل الحاصل
اجتماع النقيضين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is about God's actions or that multiple gods could exist but choose not to act.
Correction: The proof is purely logical: it shows that the very concept of multiple gods is self-contradictory, because it leads to absurd consequences. It is not about what gods might do, but about the impossibility of their existence.

Checkpoint
In the proof, what is the consequence if two gods agree to bring each thing into existence together?
A) It is permissible because both are powerful.
B) It leads to the impossibility of two effectors on one effect.
C) It results in each being incapable separately.
D) It leads to one god being submissive to the other.

Key Takeaway
The oneness of God is rationally necessary because the existence of multiple gods would make the world's existence impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof demolishes any excuse to attribute power, control, or ultimate reliance to anything besides Allah. What 'small gods'—people, possessions, status, or your own plans—do you still secretly treat as independent sources of security? When will you uproot them from your heart and declare them powerless?
?
The proof shows that if you believe in more than one ultimate reality, the world itself could not exist. Yet how often do you live as if your problems have multiple ultimate causes—your boss, your finances, your health—rather than seeing them all under Allah's sole control? What would it take to let that shift transform your anxiety into tawakkul today?
?
If you truly internalized that the Creator is one with no peer, how would you change the way you seek help, make decisions, and handle disappointment? Are you willing to test that belief right now by surrendering a specific worry to Allah alone, without any backup plan?

The Proof of Mutual Hindrance (Burhān al-Tamānu')
Sanusi recites the proof of mutual hindrance to establish divine oneness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the proof of mutual hindrance logically demonstrates that multiple gods cannot exist.

Core Idea
Two gods would always conflict, proving only one God can exist.

This lesson presents one of the most famous rational proofs for God's oneness in Islamic theology. Known as burhān al-tamānu', it shows that if there were two gods with absolute power, they would inevitably come into conflict, leading to logical absurdity. The passage from al-Sanusi's Jawharat al-Tawhid lays out this argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical structure: assumption, possibility, dilemma, conclusion.
2
Understand the assumption
The proof begins by assuming two individuals each qualified with divine attributes. Understand that this is the hypothesis to be disproved.
3
Follow the conflict scenario
Consider a simple scenario: one god wills Zayd's movement, the other his stillness. This is possible because the wills themselves are not contradictory, but the objects are.
The key point is that such a scenario is logically possible under the assumption.
4
Analyze the two outcomes
Either both objects occur (impossible because opposites can't coexist) or one fails (showing that god is incapable). Both outcomes are incompatible with divinity.
This dilemma shows the assumption leads to absurdity.
5
Connect to the conclusion
Since the assumption of multiple gods leads to logical impossibility, it must be false. Thus, God must be one. See how the Quranic verse supports this rational proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقرير برهَانِ التَّمانُع بأنَّه لو وُجِد فَرْدَان متّصفان بصفات الألوهية لأمكن بينهما تمانع ، بأن يريد أحدهما حركة زيدٍ والآخرُ سُكونَه ، لأنَّ كلَّا منهما في نفسه أمر ممكن، وكذا تعلّق الإرادة بكل منهما ؛ إذ لا تضاد بين الإرادتين ، بل بين المُرادين ؛ وحينئذ إما أن يحصل الأمران فيجتمعَ الضَّدَّان ، أو لا ، فيلزم عجز أحدهما ، أمارة الحدوث (۱) والإمكان لما فيه من شائبة الاحتياج ؛ فالتَّعدُّد مُستلزم لإمكانِ التَّمانع المُستلزم لِلْمُحال (۲) ، فيكونُ مُحالاً ، وهذا يقال له: برهان التمانع ، وإليه الإشارة بقوله تعالى: لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا عَالِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَنَا وَلَوْ [الأنبياء: ٢٢] وبيانه ما علمت.
Recitation of the proof of mutual hindrance: that if there existed two individuals qualified with the attributes of divinity, mutual hindrance would be possible between them, such that one wills the movement of Zayd and the other his stillness, because each of them is possible in itself, and likewise the attachment of will to each of them; for there is no opposition between the two wills, but rather between the two objects of will. And then either both things occur, so the two opposites would come together, or not, so the incapacity of one of them would follow, as an indication (amāra) of origination (ḥudūth) and possibility (imkān) due to what is in it of a taint of need. So multiplicity necessarily entails the possibility of mutual hindrance, which necessarily entails what is impossible, so it is impossible. And this is called the proof of mutual hindrance, and it is alluded to in His statement, exalted: 'If there were in them gods besides Allah, they would both have been corrupted' [al-Anbiya: 22], and its explanation is what you have known.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage gives a more refined version of the proof of oneness known as burhān al-tamānu' (proof of mutual hindrance). It is structured as follows:
- Assume two beings each possessing divine attributes.
- It would then be possible for them to disagree: one wills a thing, the other wills its opposite. (e.g., one wills Zayd's movement, the other his stillness). This is possible because the wills themselves are not contradictory, but the objects of will are.
- In such a scenario, either both objects occur (which would bring together two opposites, impossible), or one fails to occur (which shows that god is incapable to achieve his will).
- Thus, the possibility of mutual hindrance (tamānu') leads to either an impossible outcome or a deficiency (incapacity), which contradicts divine perfection.
- Therefore, the assumption of multiple gods is impossible.
- The passage concludes by citing the Qur'anic verse from Surah al-Anbiya: 22 as a scriptural pointer to this rational proof. The phrase 'indication (amāra) of origination and possibility' suggests that if one god is incapable, it indicates that he is originated and needy, not eternal and perfect.

Key Terms

تمانع
إرادة
ضد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mutual hindrance means the gods physically fight each other.
Correction: The proof is logical: it concerns conflicting wills and the impossibility of coordinating two unlimited powers, not physical force.

Checkpoint
What is the conclusion of the proof of mutual hindrance (برهان التمانع)?
A) Multiple gods are possible but rarely agree.
B) Multiple gods are impossible because they would necessarily hinder each other, leading to absurdity.
C) One god is sufficient, but two could exist if they never disagreed.
D) The proof shows that gods cannot will opposites, so they must be one.

Key Takeaway
The proof of mutual hindrance shows that polytheism is rationally impossible because it leads to logical contradictions or divine imperfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The proof shows that two ultimate authorities are impossible. In your daily life, what or who do you treat as a 'second authority' that competes with Allah's commands? Are you willing to identify it and submit to Allah alone?
?
If you had to honestly name one situation where you feel 'torn' between what Allah wants and what you want, what is it? How does the irrationality of two contradictory supreme wills push you toward surrender?

Burhan al-Tamani: Proof of Tawhid
Sanusi presents the proof of tawhid using the argument of mutual hindrance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the Proof of Mutual Hindrance and how it establishes the impossibility of multiple gods.

Core Idea
If two gods could exist, they could disagree—and that alone proves their impossibility.

The Proof of Mutual Hindrance is one of the most powerful logical arguments for tawhid. It shows that the mere possibility of conflict between two divine beings leads to an absurdity. Sanusi presents this argument in a clear, step-by-step form. Read the original Arabic passage below, then follow the commentary to unpack its logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then its English translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if there were two individuals...'
Pay attention to the logical connectors like 'إما أن' (either/or).
2
Identify the key assumptions
The proof assumes two beings with full divine attributes. What would be possible between them? This is the crux.
The proof does not require actual disagreement, only possibility.
3
Trace the two outcomes
The proof examines two possibilities: both wills occur (leading to combination of opposites) or one fails (leading to impotence). Both are impossible for God.
Impotence is a sign of contingency, not divinity.
4
Connect to the Quranic verse
The proof is rooted in the Quran (21:22). See how the verse alludes to this logical reasoning.
The verse says 'they would have been corrupted', which is interpreted as mutual hindrance.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that multiplicity is impossible, so God must be one in essence and attributes.
This proof is a rational demonstration of tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقرير برهان التمانع
والمراد بها هنا : وحدة الذات والصفات ، بمعنى عدم النظير فيهما.
[تقرير برهَانِ التَّمانُع]
بأنَّه لو وُجِد فَرْدَان متّصفان بصفات الألوهية لأمكن بينهما تمانع ، بأن يريد أحدهما حركة زيدٍ والآخرُ سُكونَه ، لأنَّ كلَّا منهما في نفسه أمر ممكن، وكذا تعلّق الإرادة بكل منهما ؛ إذ لا تضاد بين الإرادتين ، بل بين المُرادين ؛ وحينئذ إما أن يحصل الأمران فيجتمعَ الضَّدَّان ، أو لا ، فيلزم عجز أحدهما ، أمارة الحدوث (۱) والإمكان لما فيه من شائبة الاحتياج ؛ فالتَّعدُّد مُستلزم لإمكانِ التَّمانع المُستلزم لِلْمُحال (۲) ، فيكونُ مُحالاً ، وهذا يقال له: برهان التمانع ، وإليه الإشارة بقوله تعالى: لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا عَالِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَنَا وَلَوْ الأنبياء: ٢٢] وبيانه ما علمت.
وهو المطلوب.
Establishment of the proof of mutual hindrance. What is meant by it here is: the oneness of essence and attributes, meaning the absence of an equal in them. [Establishment of the proof of mutual hindrance] That if two individuals existed, both characterized by the attributes of divinity, mutual hindrance would be possible between them, such that one wills the motion of Zayd and the other his stillness, because each of them in itself is a possible matter, and likewise the attachment of will to each of them; for there is no opposition between the two wills, but rather between the two objects of will; and then either the two matters occur, and the two opposites would be combined, or not, and then the impotence of one of them follows, an indication of temporality (1) and possibility because of the element of need in it; so multiplicity necessitates the possibility of mutual hindrance which necessitates the impossible (2), so it is impossible, and this is called the proof of mutual hindrance, and it is alluded to by His statement, the Most High: 'If there were in them gods besides Allah, they would have been corrupted' [Surah al-Anbiya': 22], and its explanation is what you know. And that is the desired conclusion.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents the classical 'Proof of Mutual Hindrance' (Burhan al-Tamani') for the oneness of God. The author begins by stating that the intended meaning here is the oneness of essence and attributes, i.e., that God has no equal or peer. The proof itself is set up as a conditional: if there were two individuals each possessing all the attributes of divinity, then it would be possible for them to mutually hinder each other. For example, one might will that Zayd moves while the other wills that Zayd remains still. This is possible because each act of will is individually possible, and there is no direct conflict between the two wills as such, but rather between the objects of the wills. From this, two outcomes are possible: if both acts of will are realized, then both motion and stillness would exist simultaneously, combining two opposites, which is impossible. If they are not both realized, then at least one of the two fails to actualize its will, which would indicate impotence—an attribute impossible for a true deity, as it is a sign of temporality and need. Thus, the existence of multiple gods necessarily leads to impossibility, therefore it is impossible. The author notes that this proof is alluded to in the Quranic verse (21:22). He concludes that the opposite is established: that the Creator and Administrator of this universe is one in essence and attributes.

Key Terms
برهان التمانع
تمانع
التعدد
المحال
إمكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof of mutual hindrance assumes that two gods would necessarily disagree or fight each other.
Correction: The proof does not require actual disagreement; it only requires the possibility of disagreement, which is enough to lead to an impossibility.

Checkpoint
What is the key logical consequence of assuming two gods according to the proof of mutual hindrance?
A) They would always agree, so no problem arises.
B) They would necessarily fight each other.
C) The possibility of conflict leads to an impossibility (combination of opposites or impotence).
D) They would each create separate universes.

Key Takeaway
The possibility of conflict between multiple gods leads to logical impossibility, proving that God must be one.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Have you ever harbored any doubt in your heart that there might be other powers influencing your life besides Allah? How does this proof demand that you uproot any such notion and submit fully to His sole authority?
?
The proof shows that multiple wills would lead to contradiction or impotence. In your own life, when you try to serve multiple masters (desires, people, status), do you experience a similar 'mutual hindrance'? What does this proof teach you about the need for single-minded devotion to Allah?

Proof of the Necessity of Divine Power
Conditional proof for divine power based on world's existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the conditional proof for the necessity of divine power (qudra) and how it uses observation and causal reasoning.

Core Idea
The world's existence proves the Creator must have power.

This passage lays out a compact yet rigorous proof for the necessity of Allah's attribute of power. It uses a conditional syllogism: if the Creator lacked power, the world wouldn't exist. Since the world does exist, He must possess power. The commentator then justifies each premise — one by direct observation, the other by the principle that an incapable being cannot create.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure of the proof
Notice that the proof is a conditional syllogism (shartiyya istithna'iyya). The author states the if-then premise, then affirms the consequent via observation. Find each part.
The proof has three clear parts: the conditional statement, evidence for the second premise, and evidence for the implication.
2
Understand the justification of the conditional premise
The author explains why the implication holds: creation requires power because an incapable being cannot do anything. This is a rational principle.
3
Appreciate the role of observation
The second premise ('but the world exists') is proven by direct sensory experience. This anchors the proof in observable reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام على دليل وجوب القدرة له سبحانه ، فأن تقول: لو لم يجب اتصاف الله بالقدرة ، لما وُجِدَ شيءٌ من هذا العالم ، لكن هذا العالم موجود، فيثبت أنَّ الله تعالى متّصف بالقدرة، أما الدليل على صحة الاستثنائية وهي قولنا: لكن العالم موجود» فهو العيان والمشاهدة ، وأمَّا دليل الملازمة في قولنا : (لو لم يجب اتصاف الله تعالى بالقدرة ، لما وجد شيءٌ مِن هذا العالم ، فهو أنَّ الفعل الذي هو إيجاد العالم لا يصح بدون القدرة، لأن العاجز لا يقوى على فعل ما يريد، وهذا واضح إن شاء الله تعالى .
As for the discussion on the proof of the necessity of power for Him, glorified, you say: If the attribution of power to Allah were not necessary, then nothing of this world would exist. But this world exists, so it is established that Allah, exalted, is described with power. As for the proof of the correctness of the conditional statement—which is our saying 'but the world exists'—it is direct observation (al-'iyan wa al-mushahada). As for the proof of the implication in our saying: 'If the attribution of power to Allah, exalted, were not necessary, then nothing of this world would exist', it is that the act which is the creation of the world is not valid without power, because the incapable one cannot have strength to do what he intends. And this is clear, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage presents a concise logical proof for the necessity of the attribute of power (qudra) for Allah. The proof is structured as a conditional syllogism (shartiyya istithna'iyya):
1. If it were not obligatory for Allah to be described with power, then nothing of this world would exist.
2. But this world does exist.
3. Therefore, Allah is described with power.

The author then justifies the two premises. The second premise ('but the world exists') is established by direct sensory observation (al-'iyan wa al-mushahada)—we see the world around us. The first premise (the implication) is supported by reasoning: the act of creating the world requires power because an incapable being (al-'ajiz) cannot accomplish what it intends. Without power, the act of creation is impossible. Hence, the existence of the world necessarily implies the existence of power in its Creator.

The proof is straightforward and relies on a universal principle: any agent performing a deliberate act must possess the ability to do so. Since the world is a deliberate act of creation, its Creator must have power. The author concludes with 'this is clear, Allah willing', indicating the self-evident nature of the reasoning.

Key Terms
دليل وجوب القدرة
القدرة الإلهية
الاستثنائية
الملازمة
العيان والمشاهدة
العاجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is circular because it assumes what it proves.
Correction: The proof starts from an observable fact (the world's existence) and deduces an unseen attribute (power) via a necessary implication, so it is not circular.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for proving the truth of the conditional statement (ملازمة) in the proof of qudra?
A) Observation and direct witness of the world.
B) The fact that an incapable being cannot perform a deliberate act.
C) The text of revelation.
D) Consensus of scholars.

Key Takeaway
The existence of the world is sufficient proof that its Creator possesses power, because an incapable being cannot create anything.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You see the world around you every day. Do you consciously recognize each sight as a proof of Allah's power? Or do you take it for granted? What would change if you started seeing every tree and mountain as a direct evidence of His power?
?
The proof says the incapable cannot create anything. You know that you are utterly weak and incapable of creating even a single leaf. When you think about your own helplessness, how does it make you feel about your need for Allah? Do you truly rely on His power in your daily life?
?
This argument is so clear the author says 'this is clear, Allah willing.' But do you live as if it is clear? When you face difficulties, do you remember that the One who created the world with power can help you? Or do you forget and rely on your own limited strength?

Proof for the Necessity of Power in Allah
Sanusi presents a syllogistic proof that Allah must possess power based on the existence of the world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the syllogistic proof that Allah must possess power (qudra) based on the existence of the world.

Core Idea
The existence of the world is the proof that Allah possesses power.

Sanusi presents a crisp logical argument to demonstrate that the attribute of power is necessary for Allah. The proof takes the form of a conditional syllogism (shartiyya istithnāʾiyya), where the existence of the world serves as the minor premise. By analysing the two components — the observation of the world and the implication linking creation to power — the argument becomes airtight.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
2
Identify the syllogistic structure
Find the conditional statement (implication), the exceptive premise (observation), and the conclusion.
3
Examine the two sub-proofs
Note how Sanusi proves the exceptive premise by direct observation and the implication by the nature of creation requiring power.
4
Reflect on the argument's validity
Consider why this is considered a demonstrative proof in Kalam and how it avoids circularity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام على دليل وجوب القدرة له سبحانه ، فأن تقول: لو لم يجب اتصاف الله بالقدرة ، لما وُجِدَ شيءٌ من هذا العالم ، لكن هذا العالم موجود، فيثبت أنَّ الله تعالى متّصف بالقدرة، أما الدليل على صحة الاستثنائية وهي قولنا: لكن العالم موجود» فهو العيان والمشاهدة ، وأمَّا دليل الملازمة في قولنا : (لو لم يجب اتصاف الله تعالى بالقدرة ، لما وجد شيءٌ مِن هذا العالم ، فهو أنَّ الفعل الذي هو إيجاد العالم لا يصح بدون القدرة، لأن العاجز لا يقوى على فعل ما يريد، وهذا واضح إن شاء الله تعالى .
And as for the discussion on the proof of the necessity of power (qudra) for Him, exalted, you say: If it were not necessary that Allah be described with power, then nothing of this world would exist. But this world does exist, so it is established that Allah, exalted, is described with power. As for the proof of the soundness of the exceptive statement (al-istithnāʾiyya), which is our statement: 'but the world exists', it is direct observation and witnessing (al-ʿiyān wa-l-mushāhada). And as for the proof of the implication (al-mulāzama) in our statement: 'If it were not necessary that Allah, exalted, be described with power, nothing of this world would exist', it is that the act which is the bringing into existence of the world is not valid without power, because the incapable (al-ʿājiz) does not have the strength to do what he wants. And this is clear, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage provides a proof (dalīl) for the necessity of the attribute of power in Allah. The argument is formulated as a conditional syllogism (shartiyya istithnāʾiyya). It consists of a conditional premise: 'If it were not necessary that Allah be described with power, then nothing of this world would exist.' The minor premise (the exceptive statement) affirms the consequent: 'But this world does exist.' The conclusion is that Allah is indeed described with power. The author then justifies each part: the minor premise ('but the world exists') is proven by direct observation and witnessing (al-ʿiyān wa-l-mushāhada) – we see the world with our senses. The major premise (the implication) is proven by the fact that the act of creating the world cannot be performed without power, because someone incapable cannot do what he intends. This logical link is self-evident. Thus, the proof is complete.

Key Terms

وجوب القدرة
استثنائية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is circular because it assumes creation requires power.
Correction: The proof is not circular; it relies on two independent premises: the observed existence of the world and the self-evident truth that an act of creation requires power. The implication is justified by the nature of action, not by the conclusion.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The existence of the world, proven by observation, combined with the logical necessity that creation requires power, establishes that Allah possesses the attribute of power.

Proof That God Must Possess Will
Al-Sanusi gives a proof from contingency for God's will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that God must possess the attribute of will, derived from the existence of the world.

Core Idea
If God lacked will, all would be forced, yet the world exists.

Al-Sanusi now presents a concise proof that God must possess will. The argument is based on a simple conditional: if God did not have will, He would be coerced; but a coerced being could not produce the orderly world we observe. Since the world exists, God must have will. This proof mirrors the earlier one for divine power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and its translation slowly. Notice how the proof is structured as a conditional chain leading to a conclusion.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the conditional premises
Break the proof into its logical steps: (1) If no will, then coercion; (2) If coercion, then no world; (3) But world exists; therefore will is necessary.
Each step relies on the previous.
3
Reflect on the parallel to power
Al-Sanusi says this proof is like the proof for power. Consider how both attributes are derived from the contingency of the world.
4
Consider the counterargument
Read the common misunderstanding: some think the proof is circular. The commentary clarifies it starts from the observed existence of the world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الدليل على وجوب اتصاف الله تعالى بالإرادة فتقريره أن نقول: لو لم تجب له الإرادة لكان مُكرَها ، ولو كان مكرها لما وجد شيءٌ مِن هذا العالم، ولكن العالم موجود، فثبت كونه سبحانه متصفا بالإرادة ، والكلام على هذا الدليل كالكلام على دليل القدرة ، وقد تقدم قريباً.
As for the proof for the necessity of Allah Almighty possessing will, its formulation is that we say: If will were not necessary for Him, He would be coerced; and if He were coerced, nothing of this world would exist; but the world exists; so it is established that He, glorified, is characterized by will. The discussion of this proof is like the discussion of the proof of power, and it has preceded recently.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage provides a brief logical proof for the necessity of the attribute of will in God. It begins by stating the opposite: if God did not have will, He would be compelled (mukrah) — i.e., His actions would be forced, not chosen. But a coerced being cannot bring about a complex, ordered world. Since the world does exist, God must have will. The passage notes that this proof parallels the earlier proof for the attribute of power (qudrah), and that it has already been discussed.

Key Terms
إرادة
مكرَه
الدليل
وجوب
اتصاف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the proof is circular because it assumes what it tries to prove.
Correction: The proof is not circular; it starts from the observed existence of the world (a fact) and uses logical conditionals to deduce the necessity of will.

Checkpoint
What would be the case if God did not have will, according to the proof?
A) He would be unable to create.
B) He would be coerced.
C) He would not know.
D) He would be unjust.

Key Takeaway
The existence of the world logically entails that God must possess will, otherwise He would be coerced and unable to create.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The proof says that without will, God would be coerced. What would change if you recognized that your actions stem from your own will, yet are encompassed by Allah's will?
?
The world exists because Allah willed it. Does your daily schedule reflect that reality? Is there any part of your day that you live as if Allah's will is not relevant? What would it take to bring that area into alignment?

Proof of the Necessity of Life for God
Proof that God must be described with life, using the necessity of other attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the indirect proof for God's attribute of life based on the necessity of His other attributes, and how al-Ghazali argues that this is known by necessity.

Core Idea
God's life is proven indirectly through His other attributes, which require it.

This lesson presents the formal proof for the necessity of life as an attribute of God. The proof is not direct but relies on the already established attributes like power, will, and knowledge. Al-Ghazali then reinforces this with an argument from necessity, defining 'living' as that which is self-aware and knowing. Understanding this proof helps us see the interconnectedness of the divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the structure: first the formal proof, then al-Ghazali's statement.
The proof uses a conditional argument (if... then...).
2
Identify the proof's logic
The proof says: if God were not alive, He could not have power, will, knowledge, etc. Since those attributes are already proven, life must be proven too. This is an indirect proof by necessity.
3
Examine al-Ghazali's argument
Al-Ghazali says that life is known by necessity to anyone who admits God is knowing and powerful. He defines 'living' as that which is aware of itself and knows itself and others. Since God knows all and has power over all, He must be alive.
This is a conceptual argument: the meaning of 'living' entails awareness and knowledge.
4
Reflect on the definition of life
Consider the definition: 'living' means being aware of oneself and knowing one's essence and others. How does this definition apply to God? How does it connect to the proof?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ - صفة الحياة، تعريفها، ودليل وجوبها له تعالى
وأما الكلام على دليل وجوب اتصافه الله بالحياة فنقول : لو لم يجب أن يتصف بالحياة لما صح أنْ يتّصفَ بالقدرة والإرادة والعلم وغيرها من الصفات، لكن اتصافه تعالى بهذه الصفات ثابت بالدليل الذي أقمناه على وجوب اتصافه بكل واحدة منها ، فيثبت كونه تعالى واجبا له الاتصاف بالحياة.
قال حجة الإسلام الغزالي: واتصافه تعالى بالحياة معلوم بالضرورة، ولم ينكره أحدٌ ممَّن اعترَفَ بكونه تعالى عالماً ، قادرًا ، فإنَّ كونَ العالِم القادرِ حيًّا ضروري ؛ إذ لا نعني بالحي إلا ما يشعر بنفسه ويعلم ذاته وغيره، والعالم بجميع المعلومات، والقادر على جميع المقدورات، كيف لا يكون حيًّا ؟! وهذا واضح والنَّظر في صفة الحياة لا يطول» اهـ . 4 - The attribute of life, its definition, and the proof of its necessity for Him Most High. As for the speech on the proof of the necessity of His being described with life, we say: If it were not necessary for Him to be described with life, then it would not be correct for Him to be described with power, will, knowledge, and other attributes. But His being described with these attributes is established by the proof we have established for the necessity of His being described with each one of them. Thus it is established that He Most High is necessarily described with life. The Proof of Islam al-Ghazali said: 'His being described with life is known by necessity, and not one who acknowledges that He Most High is knowing and powerful has denied it. For the knowing, powerful being being alive is necessary, since we do not mean by 'living' except that which is aware of itself and knows its essence and other things. And He is knowing of all known things and powerful over all possible things, how could He not be alive? This is clear, and reflection on the attribute of life is not lengthy.' End.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage provides a formal proof (dalil) for the necessity of life as an attribute of God. The proof is indirect: if God were not alive, He could not be described with power, will, knowledge, or other attributes that have already been proven for Him. Since those attributes are established, it follows necessarily that life is also established. The passage then cites al-Ghazali, who argues that God's life is known by necessity (darura) and is not denied by anyone who admits that God is knowing and powerful. Al-Ghazali defines 'living' (hayy) as that which is aware of itself and knows its essence and others. Since God is knowing of all things and powerful over all things, He must be alive. This is presented as self-evident.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the proof of God's life is direct (e.g., from the need for a creator to be living).
Correction: The proof is indirect: it relies on other attributes (power, will, knowledge) that already require life as a precondition.

Checkpoint
According to the proof presented, why must God be described with life?
A) Because life is logically prior to all other attributes
B) Because without life, God could not have power, will, or knowledge, which are already proven
C) Because al-Ghazali said so
D) Because life is a necessary consequence of existence

Key Takeaway
God's life is necessary because without it, the other attributes proven for Him could not exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

You claim to believe that God has power, will, and knowledge. The lesson shows that these attributes necessitate His life. So, if He is alive, then He hears your prayers, sees your struggles, and responds. What is one prayer you have been hesitant to make because you doubted He would answer? Will you pray it now, with full confidence in His living power?

The Impossible Attributes of Allah (Third Division)
Enumeration of impossible attributes with definition of 'opposite'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the categories of attributes that are impossible for Allah and why the linguistic meaning of 'opposite' is used here.

Core Idea
The impossible attributes of Allah are the opposites of His necessary attributes.

This lesson continues the rational judgment division. After covering necessary and possible attributes, Sanusi now discusses what is impossible for Allah. Understanding these impossible attributes reinforces the transcendence of Allah and guards against anthropomorphism and associating partners with Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get an overview of the impossible attributes listed. Then read the translation to understand the details.
Notice that each impossible attribute is defined as the opposite of a necessary attribute.
2
Understand the meaning of 'opposite'
Pay attention to the commentary's distinction between the customary and linguistic meanings of 'opposite'. Why is the linguistic meaning intended here?
The linguistic meaning applies to both existent and non-existent opposites.
3
Identify the impossible attributes
List each impossible attribute mentioned: non-existence, origination, annihilation, similarity, dependency, and lack of oneness. Note their corresponding necessary attributes.
Reflect on how each impossibility protects the concept of tawhid.

۳۱۹
The third division of the rational judgments: what is impossible for Him, Exalted. 43 - And the opposite of the one with attributes is impossible in His truth, like being in directions.
What is impossible for Him, Exalted.
Allah, the possible, and the impossible.
..
And it is what is impossible in His right. So he said: (And) it is legally obligatory (1) to believe that (it is impossible) for Him, Exalted, (the opposite of the one with attributes (2)).
(1) His saying: 'And it is legally obligatory' meaning by the Law, or from the perspective of the Law. And this division – there is no doubt about its knowledge – is in the obligation of the first division for Him, Exalted. He only mentioned it in the manner of the people in their inclination to the signification of mutabaqah (correspondence) and their turning away from the signification of tadammun (inclusion) and iltizam (concomitance) in matters of beliefs, avoiding ignorance as much as possible; because the one who errs in them is sinful even if he exerted effort in matters of beliefs, unlike in furu' (subsidiary matters). (Shanwani) (2) 'Opposite' has two meanings: one customary and the other linguistic. As for its customary meaning, it is 'the existent thing that does not coincide with its opposite, and both it and its opposite can be absent.' This meaning is not intended here because among the opposites impossible for Him, Exalted, are those that are not existent, like annihilation. As for the linguistic meaning: 'opposite' linguistically applies to any contradiction, whether existent or non-existent. This is the meaning intended here.
Thus, non-existence is impossible for Him, Exalted, and it is the opposite of existence; origination is impossible for Him, and it is the opposite of eternity; annihilation, i.e., the occurrence of non-existence, is impossible for Him, and it is the opposite of everlastingness; similarity to originated things is impossible for Him, and it is the opposite of being unlike originated things. The impossible similarity is conceived as being a body, whether it is composite called a body or non-composite called an individual substance, or as being an accident subsisting in a body, or as being in a direction of a body: He is not above the Throne, nor beneath it, nor to its right, nor to its left, removed from that. You have known the doctrine of the Salaf and Khalaf in explaining the meaning of His statement: 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne' (Taha:5), or as being in a place or being temporally delimited. We have detailed that in the discourse on establishing His being unlike originated things. And it is impossible for Him not to be self-subsisting, i.e., to need a substrate in which He subsists or a specifier; that is the opposite of His self-subsistence. And it is impossible for Him not to be one, i.e., to be composite in His essence, or to have a similar in His essence, or to have multiplicity in His attributes of a single type, like two powers or two wills, or for someone to have an attribute resembling His attribute, or for there to be with Him in existence an influence in any action. All of this is the opposite of oneness (wahdaniyya).
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a classification and enumeration. It begins by stating the third division of rational judgments: what is impossible for Him. The verse says that the opposite of the one with attributes is impossible, like being in directions. The commentator then explains the meaning of 'opposite' (didd) in detail, distinguishing between the customary meaning (which only applies to existents) and the linguistic meaning (which applies to both existential and non-existential opposites). Since some of the impossible attributes are non-existential (like non-existence), the linguistic meaning is intended. The passage then enumerates several impossible attributes: non-existence (opposite of existence), origination (opposite of eternity), annihilation (opposite of everlastingness), similarity to originated things (opposite of being unlike them). Similarity is further explained as being composite (a body), being an accident, being in a direction, etc. The commentator also references the salaf-khalaf discussion on the throne verse. Then it lists being in need of a substrate (opposite of self-subsistence), and lacking oneness (being composite, having a similar, having multiple attributes of the same type, having a partner in existence). This enumeration covers the main categories of impossible attributes.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'opposite' only refers to existent things, so non-existence and annihilation cannot be opposites.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the linguistic meaning of 'opposite' includes non‑existent contradictions, so non‑existence is still a valid opposite of existence.

Key Takeaway
The impossible attributes of Allah are the opposites of His necessary attributes, reinforcing divine transcendence and oneness.

Are you guilty of letting these descriptions become literal images in your mind?
