The Two Qadariyya Sects and Refutation of the First
The author describes two Qadariyya sects and refutes the first.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the beliefs of the two Qadariyya sects and why the first is refuted as kufr.

Core Idea
The Qadariyya are named for their extreme denial, not affirmation, of divine decree.

The author begins by introducing a sect that denied God's eternal knowledge, then another that claimed humans create their own actions. This lesson clarifies their distinct beliefs and why the first sect's doctrine is considered disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the first Qadariyya
Read the Arabic text describing the first sect's belief and the reason for their naming.
Notice the linguistic point about attribution due to denial.
2
Identify the second Qadariyya
Find the description of the Mu'tazila sect and their claim that the slave creates his actions.
3
Distinguish the two sects
The passage explicitly says the author refutes the first, not the second. Understand why the second's refutation is elsewhere.
The second sect affirmed God's eternal knowledge but disagreed on human agency.
4
Reflect on the naming irony
Consider why they are called Qadariyya despite denying qadr.
The author explains it is due to their extreme denial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقبل أن نتحدث إليك عن هذه المسألة، وأنْ نُبَيِّن رأي أهل السنة والجماعة فيها، والدليل الذي استندوا إليه في تدعيم مذهبهم نُبيّن لك أنَّ فرقةً تزْعُم الانتساب إلى الإسلام كانت تقول: إن الله تعالى لم يُقدِّر الأمور أزلا ، وإِنَّ الأمر أُنف - بضم الهمزة والنون جميعا ـ ، أي: يستأنف الله تعالى علمه حال وقوعه، وقد سمَّاهم أهل السنة والجماعة «القدرية» ومعنى هذه النسبة: الجماعة المنسوبون إلى القدر، وإنَّما نسبوهم إلى القدر - مع كونهم ينفونه ولا يقولون به ـ ؛ لأنهم لمَّا بالغوا في نفيه وجعلوا ذلك النَّفي نحلة لهم واتخذوه دَيْدَنا صح أن يُنسبوا إليه ، ولا يلزمُ من نسبةِ أحدٍ إلى شيء أن يكون وجه نسبته إليه أنه مثبت له ، بل كما تكون النسبة إلى الشيء بسبب إثباته .. تكونُ النّسبة إليه بسبب نفيه ، خصوصاً إذا بالغ في النَّفي وجعل النَّفِي هَجِيرَاهُ. وثمَّةَ فِرقة أخرى أطلقوا عليها اسم «القدرية» أيضاً، وهذه الفرقة الأخرى إحدى فرق المعتزلة ، وهم الذين قالوا: إن العبد خالق لأفعال نفسه الاختيارية ، وهذا الفريق مجمع ـ مع أهل السنة - على أنَّ الله تعالى عالم بأفعال العباد أزلاً قبل وقوعها منهم، ومن هنا تَعلَم أَنَّ اسم «القدرية» يطلق عند أهل الكلام على فرقتين: أما إحداهما: فطائفةٌ نَفتْ علم الله تعالى أزلا بأفعال العباد، وزعمت أنه لا يعلمها إلا حال وقوعها، وللتمييز بينها وبين الطائفة الأخرى أُطلق عليها اسم «القدرية الأولى» ومُعتقد هذه الطائفة كفرُ عند أهل السنة والجماعة ، ويذكر العلماء أنَّ هذه الطائفة قد انقرضت ولم يبقَ من يذهب مذهبها قبل انقضاء القرن الثاني الهجري. وأما الأخرى فطائفةٌ من المعتزلة ، وهم يعترفون بأنَّ الله تعالى يعلم أفعال العباد قبل وقوعها، يعلمها أزلاً قبل أن يخلق الخلق، ولكنَّهم قالوا العبد خالقُ أفعال نفسه الاختيارية، وهذه الطائفة تسمى «القدريَّة الثَّانية» تمييزاً بينها وبين الطائفة الأولى. إذا علمت هذا على هذا البيان فنقول : أراد المصنف بهذا الكلام الرَّدَّ على القدرية الأُولى، ولم يُرِدْ به الرَّدَّ على القدرية الثانية ؛ لأنَّ الرَّدَّ على القدرية الثانية قد مضى في قوله: «وخَالِقٌ لعَبْدِه ومَا عَمِل وفي قوله : (وَعِنْدَنَا للعَبْدِ كَسْبٌ كُلفا به». وقد بين الشارح - ه - معنى القَدَرِ عند الأشاعرة والماتريدية ، وبيَّن أنه ليس بين الفريقين خلاف حقيقي ، وإنما الخلاف في العبارة التي دلّ بها كل فريق على مراده، فأما المعنى فهم على اتفاق فيه. وخلاصة ما ذهب إليه أهل السنة والجماعة في هذه المسألة: أنَّه يجب على المُكلَّف أنْ يؤمن بأنَّ الله سبحانه عَلِم أزلا بجميع أفعال العباد ، وأنه أوجَدَها ـ حين أوجدها فيما لا يزال ـ على القَدْرِ المَخصُوص والوَجْه المُعيَّن الذي سبق العلم به ، بل إنَّ ذلك ممَّا لا يتحقَّقُ الإيمان إلا به ، والدليل على ذلك أنَّ النبيَّ الله لما بيَّن لجبريل الإيمان ـ سواء قلنا إنه بين حقيقة الإيمان بناءً على أنَّ الأعمال جزء منه، أو قلنا إنَّه إنَّما بيَّن خِصال الإيمان، أي: مُتعلّق الإيمان - ذَكَرَ الإيمان بالقضاء والقدر في ضمن ذلك، وذلك قوله: الإيمان أن تؤمن بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله، والقضاء والقدر، خيره وشره، وحلوه ومره .
Before we speak to you about this matter and clarify the view of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a concerning it and the proof they rely on to support their doctrine, we will clarify to you that a sect claiming affiliation with Islam used to say: God did not apportion matters from eternity, and rather the matter is 'unf' — with damma on both hamza and nun — meaning: God's knowledge is renewed at the time of occurrence. Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a called them 'al-Qadariyya'. The meaning of this attribution is: the group attributed to al-qadr (divine decree). They were attributed to al-qadr even though they deny it and do not affirm it, because when they exaggerated in denying it and made that denial a creed for themselves and took it as a habit, it is valid that they be attributed to it. It is not necessary that a person's attribution to something implies that he affirms it; rather, just as attribution to something can be due to affirming it, it can be due to denying it, especially if one exaggerates in denial and makes denial his constant practice. There is another sect also called 'al-Qadariyya'. This other sect is one of the sects of the Mu'tazila, and they said: The slave is the creator of his own voluntary actions. This group agrees with Ahl al-Sunna that God knows the actions of the slaves from eternity before they occur. From this you learn that the name 'al-Qadariyya' is applied by the people of kalam to two sects: As for one: a group that denied God's knowledge of the actions of the slaves from eternity, and claimed that He only knows them at the time of their occurrence. To distinguish it from the other sect, it is called 'the first Qadariyya'. The belief of this sect is disbelief according to Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. Scholars mention that this sect became extinct and no one followed its doctrine before the end of the second century AH. As for the other: a group from the Mu'tazila who acknowledge that God knows the actions of the slaves before they occur, knows them from eternity before He created creation, but they said: the slave is the creator of his own voluntary actions. This sect is called 'the second Qadariyya' to distinguish it from the first sect. When you know this according to this explanation, we say: The author intended by this speech the refutation of the first Qadariyya, and he did not intend by it the refutation of the second Qadariyya, because the refutation of the second Qadariyya has already passed in his statement: 'And He is the Creator of His slave and what he did' and in his statement: 'And with us, the slave has acquisition (kasb) which he is tasked with.' The commentator has explained the meaning of al-qadr according to the Ash'aris and the Maturidis, and clarified that there is no real difference between the two groups; rather the difference is in the expression by which each group indicates its intention; as for the meaning, they are in agreement. The summary of what Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a hold on this matter is: It is obligatory for the legally responsible person to believe that God knew from eternity all the actions of the slaves, and that He brought them into existence — when He brought them into existence in what will be — according to the specific measure and the particular manner that preceded knowledge with. Indeed, belief is not realized except by that. The proof for that is that the Prophet, when he explained faith (iman) to Jibril — whether we say he explained the reality of faith based on the view that actions are part of it, or we say he only explained the characteristics of faith, i.e., the objects of faith — he mentioned belief in al-qada and al-qadr within that, and that is his statement: 'Faith is that you believe in God, His angels, His books, His messengers, and al-qada and al-qadr, its good and its evil, its sweet and its bitter.'
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya sects and an affirmation of the Ahl al-Sunna position on divine decree. The author begins by introducing a sect that denied God's eternal determination and claimed that His knowledge is renewed at the moment of occurrence. They are called 'Qadariyya' despite denying qadr, because they exaggerated in denial. Then a second sect, the Mu'tazila, affirmed God's eternal knowledge but claimed that the slave creates his own actions. Both are refuted: the first by labeling their belief as disbelief (kufr) and noting its extinction; the second is already refuted earlier in the text. The commentator then clarifies that Ash'aris and Maturidis agree on the meaning of qadr despite differences in expression. Finally, the Ahl al-Sunna position is summarized: it is obligatory to believe that God knew all actions from eternity and created them according to that knowledge. The proof is the hadith of Jibril where belief in qada and qadr is explicitly mentioned as part of iman.

الجماعة
علم أزلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Qadariyya are the same and all are refuted in this passage.
Correction: There are two Qadariyya sects; the author refutes only the first (denying God's knowledge) here; the second is refuted elsewhere.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the two Qadariyya sects does the author intend to refute here?
A) The first Qadariyya who denied God's eternal knowledge
B) The second Qadariyya who affirmed God's knowledge but said the slave creates his actions
C) Both sects equally
D) Neither; he is simply explaining the meaning of qadr

Key Takeaway
The first Qadariyya sects denied God's eternal knowledge, and their belief is considered disbelief; they are called Qadariyya due to their extreme denial of qadr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever acted as if Allah does not know what you are doing—perhaps by sinning in secret or ignoring His awareness? How does the first Qadariyya's denial of God's knowledge challenge you to live with constant consciousness that He sees and knows everything, even your innermost thoughts?
?
The author says the Qadariyya made denial of qadr their 'constant practice.' What is one belief or habit you cling to that might be an exaggeration in the opposite direction—affirming something so strongly that it leads to imbalance in your faith? How can you seek the middle path of Ahl al-Sunna?
?
This lesson shows that a sect's belief was declared kufr and became extinct. Are there any modern ideologies or ideas you have passively accepted that contradict core Islamic teachings? What would it take for you to actively reject them even if they are popular?

Ahl al-Sunna's Belief in Qadr and Its Proof
The author states the obligatory Ahl al-Sunna belief in qadr and provides the hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna position on divine decree and the proof from the hadith of Jibril.

Core Idea
Belief in qada and qadr is an integral part of iman, based on explicit prophetic teaching.

After refuting the first Qadariyya, the author presents the positive belief of Ahl al-Sunna. He summarizes their doctrine: God's eternal knowledge and creation according to that knowledge, and provides the proof from the hadith of Jibril where belief in qada and qadr is listed as a pillar of iman.

Guided Path
1
Read the summary of Ahl al-Sunna belief
Read the Arabic text starting from 'وخلاصة ما ذهب إليه أهل السنة' to the end. Understand the obligatory belief.
2
Identify the proof
The author cites the hadith of Jibril. Note how belief in qada and qadr is explicitly mentioned.
The hadith is a core proof for the necessity of belief in qadr.
3
Reflect on the commentator's note
The commentator mentions that Ash'aris and Maturidis agree on the meaning despite different expressions.
This shows unity among Sunni schools.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقبل أن نتحدث إليك عن هذه المسألة، وأنْ نُبَيِّن رأي أهل السنة والجماعة فيها، والدليل الذي استندوا إليه في تدعيم مذهبهم نُبيّن لك أنَّ فرقةً تزْعُم الانتساب إلى الإسلام كانت تقول: إن الله تعالى لم يُقدِّر الأمور أزلا ، وإِنَّ الأمر أُنف - بضم الهمزة والنون جميعا ـ ، أي: يستأنف الله تعالى علمه حال وقوعه، وقد سمَّاهم أهل السنة والجماعة «القدرية» ومعنى هذه النسبة: الجماعة المنسوبون إلى القدر، وإنَّما نسبوهم إلى القدر - مع كونهم ينفونه ولا يقولون به ـ ؛ لأنهم لمَّا بالغوا في نفيه وجعلوا ذلك النَّفي نحلة لهم واتخذوه دَيْدَنا صح أن يُنسبوا إليه ، ولا يلزمُ من نسبةِ أحدٍ إلى شيء أن يكون وجه نسبته إليه أنه مثبت له ، بل كما تكون النسبة إلى الشيء بسبب إثباته .. تكونُ النّسبة إليه بسبب نفيه ، خصوصاً إذا بالغ في النَّفي وجعل النَّفِي هَجِيرَاهُ. وثمَّةَ فِرقة أخرى أطلقوا عليها اسم «القدرية» أيضاً، وهذه الفرقة الأخرى إحدى فرق المعتزلة ، وهم الذين قالوا: إن العبد خالق لأفعال نفسه الاختيارية ، وهذا الفريق مجمع ـ مع أهل السنة - على أنَّ الله تعالى عالم بأفعال العباد أزلاً قبل وقوعها منهم، ومن هنا تَعلَم أَنَّ اسم «القدرية» يطلق عند أهل الكلام على فرقتين: أما إحداهما: فطائفةٌ نَفتْ علم الله تعالى أزلا بأفعال العباد، وزعمت أنه لا يعلمها إلا حال وقوعها، وللتمييز بينها وبين الطائفة الأخرى أُطلق عليها اسم «القدرية الأولى» ومُعتقد هذه الطائفة كفرُ عند أهل السنة والجماعة ، ويذكر العلماء أنَّ هذه الطائفة قد انقرضت ولم يبقَ من يذهب مذهبها قبل انقضاء القرن الثاني الهجري. وأما الأخرى فطائفةٌ من المعتزلة ، وهم يعترفون بأنَّ الله تعالى يعلم أفعال العباد قبل وقوعها، يعلمها أزلاً قبل أن يخلق الخلق، ولكنَّهم قالوا العبد خالقُ أفعال نفسه الاختيارية، وهذه الطائفة تسمى «القدريَّة الثَّانية» تمييزاً بينها وبين الطائفة الأولى. إذا علمت هذا على هذا البيان فنقول : أراد المصنف بهذا الكلام الرَّدَّ على القدرية الأُولى، ولم يُرِدْ به الرَّدَّ على القدرية الثانية ؛ لأنَّ الرَّدَّ على القدرية الثانية قد مضى في قوله: «وخَالِقٌ لعَبْدِه ومَا عَمِل وفي قوله : (وَعِنْدَنَا للعَبْدِ كَسْبٌ كُلفا به». وقد بين الشارح - ه - معنى القَدَرِ عند الأشاعرة والماتريدية ، وبيَّن أنه ليس بين الفريقين خلاف حقيقي ، وإنما الخلاف في العبارة التي دلّ بها كل فريق على مراده، فأما المعنى فهم على اتفاق فيه. وخلاصة ما ذهب إليه أهل السنة والجماعة في هذه المسألة: أنَّه يجب على المُكلَّف أنْ يؤمن بأنَّ الله سبحانه عَلِم أزلا بجميع أفعال العباد ، وأنه أوجَدَها ـ حين أوجدها فيما لا يزال ـ على القَدْرِ المَخصُوص والوَجْه المُعيَّن الذي سبق العلم به ، بل إنَّ ذلك ممَّا لا يتحقَّقُ الإيمان إلا به ، والدليل على ذلك أنَّ النبيَّ الله لما بيَّن لجبريل الإيمان ـ سواء قلنا إنه بين حقيقة الإيمان بناءً على أنَّ الأعمال جزء منه، أو قلنا إنَّه إنَّما بيَّن خِصال الإيمان، أي: مُتعلّق الإيمان - ذَكَرَ الإيمان بالقضاء والقدر في ضمن ذلك، وذلك قوله: الإيمان أن تؤمن بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله، والقضاء والقدر، خيره وشره، وحلوه ومره .
Before we speak to you about this matter and clarify the view of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a concerning it and the proof they rely on to support their doctrine, we will clarify to you that a sect claiming affiliation with Islam used to say: God did not apportion matters from eternity, and rather the matter is 'unf' — with damma on both hamza and nun — meaning: God's knowledge is renewed at the time of occurrence. Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a called them 'al-Qadariyya'. The meaning of this attribution is: the group attributed to al-qadr (divine decree). They were attributed to al-qadr even though they deny it and do not affirm it, because when they exaggerated in denying it and made that denial a creed for themselves and took it as a habit, it is valid that they be attributed to it. It is not necessary that a person's attribution to something implies that he affirms it; rather, just as attribution to something can be due to affirming it, it can be due to denying it, especially if one exaggerates in denial and makes denial his constant practice. There is another sect also called 'al-Qadariyya'. This other sect is one of the sects of the Mu'tazila, and they said: The slave is the creator of his own voluntary actions. This group agrees with Ahl al-Sunna that God knows the actions of the slaves from eternity before they occur. From this you learn that the name 'al-Qadariyya' is applied by the people of kalam to two sects: As for one: a group that denied God's knowledge of the actions of the slaves from eternity, and claimed that He only knows them at the time of their occurrence. To distinguish it from the other sect, it is called 'the first Qadariyya'. The belief of this sect is disbelief according to Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. Scholars mention that this sect became extinct and no one followed its doctrine before the end of the second century AH. As for the other: a group from the Mu'tazila who acknowledge that God knows the actions of the slaves before they occur, knows them from eternity before He created creation, but they said: the slave is the creator of his own voluntary actions. This sect is called 'the second Qadariyya' to distinguish it from the first sect. When you know this according to this explanation, we say: The author intended by this speech the refutation of the first Qadariyya, and he did not intend by it the refutation of the second Qadariyya, because the refutation of the second Qadariyya has already passed in his statement: 'And He is the Creator of His slave and what he did' and in his statement: 'And with us, the slave has acquisition (kasb) which he is tasked with.' The commentator has explained the meaning of al-qadr according to the Ash'aris and the Maturidis, and clarified that there is no real difference between the two groups; rather the difference is in the expression by which each group indicates its intention; as for the meaning, they are in agreement. The summary of what Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a hold on this matter is: It is obligatory for the legally responsible person to believe that God knew from eternity all the actions of the slaves, and that He brought them into existence — when He brought them into existence in what will be — according to the specific measure and the particular manner that preceded knowledge with. Indeed, belief is not realized except by that. The proof for that is that the Prophet, when he explained faith (iman) to Jibril — whether we say he explained the reality of faith based on the view that actions are part of it, or we say he only explained the characteristics of faith, i.e., the objects of faith — he mentioned belief in al-qada and al-qadr within that, and that is his statement: 'Faith is that you believe in God, His angels, His books, His messengers, and al-qada and al-qadr, its good and its evil, its sweet and its bitter.'
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya sects and an affirmation of the Ahl al-Sunna position on divine decree. The author begins by introducing a sect that denied God's eternal determination and claimed that His knowledge is renewed at the moment of occurrence. They are called 'Qadariyya' despite denying qadr, because they exaggerated in denial. Then a second sect, the Mu'tazila, affirmed God's eternal knowledge but claimed that the slave creates his own actions. Both are refuted: the first by labeling their belief as disbelief (kufr) and noting its extinction; the second is already refuted earlier in the text. The commentator then clarifies that Ash'aris and Maturidis agree on the meaning of qadr despite differences in expression. Finally, the Ahl al-Sunna position is summarized: it is obligatory to believe that God knew all actions from eternity and created them according to that knowledge. The proof is the hadith of Jibril where belief in qada and qadr is explicitly mentioned as part of iman.

Key Terms
إيمان
قضاء
قدر
علم أزلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Belief in qada and qadr is not an essential part of iman.
Correction: The Prophet explicitly included it in the definition of iman in the hadith of Jibril.

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof the author gives for the obligation to believe in qada and qadr?
A) The consensus of Ahl al-Sunna
B) The hadith of Jibril
C) Rational argument
D) The extinction of the first Qadariyya

Key Takeaway
Belief in qada and qadr, both good and evil, is an integral part of iman, as proven by the hadith of Jibril.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every good and evil that happens to you is from Allah, or do you secretly attribute some events to luck or your own cleverness? How would your anxiety change if you lived every moment with this belief?
?
When you find yourself making excuses for sin by saying 'it was my qadr,' do you realize that the same Prophet who taught us to believe in qadr also taught us to strive and repent? How will you reconcile qadr with personal responsibility starting today?
?
The Prophet placed belief in qadr among the very core of iman. If you were to re-prioritize your religious learning and practice to reflect this, what is one specific change you will make this week?

The Shahadatayn Encompass All Obligatory Beliefs
Explains how the shahadatayn contain all obligatory beliefs about God and prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the two testimonies of Islam encapsulate all obligatory beliefs about God and the prophets, and how these beliefs are categorized into necessary, possible, and impossible.

Core Idea
The shahada contains all essential beliefs about God and prophets in three rational categories.

This passage from the commentary unpacks a dense line of poetry to reveal a profound truth about the shahadatayn. It shows that the first testimony affirms God's divinity, and together they cover every obligatory belief regarding God and His messengers, organized into the three rational judgments of necessity, possibility, and impossibility. Let's explore how this works.

Guided Path
1
Encounter the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the poetic line and the explanatory prose. This is an advanced commentary tradition.
The passage builds on a previous line; the poet is explaining comprehensiveness.
2
Unpack 'what was established'
The phrase 'الَّذِي تَقَرَّرَا' is explained as all obligatory beliefs. Identify what these beliefs relate to: divinity and prophethood.
These are the two main areas of theology covered by the shahada.
3
Grasp the three rational categories
The beliefs are divided into wajib (necessary), ja'iz (possible), and mustahil (impossible). These are applied to both God and prophets. For example, it is necessary for God to exist, possible for prophets to have miracles, impossible for God to have a partner.
This tripartite division is foundational in Islamic theology (kalam).
4
Understand the grammatical explanations
The phrase 'شَهَادَنَا الإِسْلَام' is interpreted as three types of idafah (annexation): part-to-whole, cause-to-effect, or indicator-to-indicated. Each highlights a different relation between the shahadatayn and Islam.
This shows the depth of linguistic analysis in Islamic scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان تضمُّنِ الشَّهادتين لجميع العقائد الإيمانيَّة الوَاجِبة.
وجَامِعٌ مَعْنى الَّذِي تَقَرَّرَا شَهادنَا الإِسْلامِ فَاطْرَحِ المِرَا.
ثُمَّ شرع في بيان ما أجمله مِن المنطوق به في قوله: «والنُّطْقُ فِيهِ الخُلْفُ» فقال: (وَجَامِعٌ مَعْنَى) وهو : ما يُراد مِن اللَّفظ (الَّذِي تَقَرَّرَا) أي جُعِلَ في قرارٍ ومحل يُرجع إليه فيه ، وهو جميع العقائد الإيمانية الواجبة الاعتقادِ شرعاً ، ممَّا يَرجعُ إلى الألوهية والنُّبوَّة وجوبا وجوازا واستحالة، شَهَادَنَا الإِسْلَام) أي : معنى الشَّهادتين اللتين هما الجزء الأعظم مِن مُسمَّى الإسلام ، أو اللتين لا يحصل الإسلام إلَّا بهما، أو اللتين تدلان على الإسلام؛ فهو من إضافة الجزء للكُلِّ ، أو السَّبب للمُسبَّب، أو الدَّال للمدلول ، وبيان ما ذكره: أنَّ الجملة الأولى أثبتت الألوهية له تعالى،
An explanation of the two testimonies encompassing all obligatory beliefs. And a comprehensive meaning of what was established — our two testimonies of Islam, so abandon disputation. Then he began to explain what he summarized from the spoken in his saying: 'And the speech in it is differ...' so he said: (And a comprehensive meaning) i.e., what is intended from the word (which was established) i.e., placed in a settled place to which reference is made, and it is all the obligatory beliefs by law, which relate to divinity and prophethood in terms of necessity, possibility, and impossibility. (Our two testimonies of Islam) i.e., the meaning of the two testimonies which are the greatest part of the name of Islam, or those without which Islam is not obtained, or those which indicate Islam; so it is an addition of the part to the whole, or the cause to the effect, or the indicator to the indicated. And an explanation of what he mentioned: that the first sentence affirmed divinity for Him, Most High,
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line of poetry stating that the two testimonies (shahadatayn) encompass all obligatory beliefs. It begins by providing the line: 'And a comprehensive meaning of what was established — our two testimonies of Islam, so abandon disputation.' Then it explains that 'what was established' (الَّذِي تَقَرَّرَا) means the meaning that is placed in a settled place (the mind or the text) and refers to all obligatory beliefs about divinity (uluhiyyah) and prophethood (nubuwwah), divided into three categories: necessary (wajib), possible (ja'iz), and impossible (mustahil). Next, it interprets 'our two testimonies of Islam' (شَهَادَنَا الإِسْلَام) in three ways: either they are the greatest part of the name 'Islam', or they are the two without which Islam is not obtained, or they are the indicators of Islam. It then relates these interpretations to grammatical constructs of idafah (annexation): part-to-whole, cause-to-effect, or indicator-to-indicated. Finally, it begins to unpack the meaning by stating that the first testimony (La ilaha illa Allah) affirms divinity (uluhiyyah) for God.

عقائد إيمانية
ألوهية
نبوة
وجوب
جواز
استحالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the shahada only affirms monotheism (tawhid) and does not include beliefs about prophethood or other matters.
Correction: This passage shows that the shahadatayn encompass all obligatory beliefs, including those about prophethood, and are categorized into necessary, possible, and impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the word 'الَّذِي تَقَرَّرَا' (what was established) refer to?
A) The two testimonies
B) All obligatory beliefs about God and prophets
C) The Quran
D) The Prophet's sunnah

Key Takeaway
The two testimonies of Islam contain all obligatory beliefs about God and prophets, categorized into necessary, possible, and impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the shahada, do you consciously affirm every obligatory belief about God and the Prophet, or have you reduced it to a mere formula? What would change if you truly meant every implication of those words?
?
The shahada requires you to believe in both necessary and possible attributes of God. Which of God's attributes do you think about most? Which do you neglect? How would your daily awareness of God shift if you actively considered His impossible attributes as well?
?
If the shahada encompasses all beliefs, does your life reflect that? Identify one belief from this lesson that you hold theoretically but do not practice. What concrete step will you take this week to act on it?

The Seal of Prophethood and Universal Mission
The author explains the seal of prophethood and universal mission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet Muhammad is the seal of all prophets and messengers, and why his mission is universal to all creation.

Core Idea
Muhammad is the final prophet sent to every being from Adam to the end of time.

This passage addresses two essential beliefs: the finality of prophethood and the universal scope of the Prophet's mission. The author explains that being the seal means no new prophet or law comes after him, and that his message is for all obligated beings—humans, jinn, and even angels. Through Quranic verses and hadith, the text establishes that Muhammad is the culmination of all previous prophethood and the messenger to all creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument come through before you interpret.
The passage includes a footnote from al-Bajuri that clarifies the spiritual dimension.
2
Understand the logic of sealing
Notice the logical argument: sealing the general (prophets) necessarily seals the specific (messengers). Grasp why no new law can come after Muhammad.
This guards against the misconception that Jesus will bring a new law.
3
Recognize the universal mission
Identify whom the Prophet was sent to: humans, jinn, Gog and Magog, and even angels. Note the hadith that confirms he was sent to all creation.
The footnote explains that even previous prophets are included in a spiritual sense.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider what these two doctrines mean for Islamic faith and law. Think about why finality and universality are foundational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إرساله إلى الملائكة
حدا ولا عدا (١) ، ولكنَّ المُهمَّ منه أَنْ قَدْ تَمَّما بِه الجَمِيعَ (٢) رَبُّنَا ) أي : خَتم ربُّنا بنبوته جميع الأنبياء ، قال تعالى: ﴿وَخَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّنَ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٤٠] . ويلزمُ منه ختم المرسلين أيضًا ؛ لأنَّ ختم الأعم ختم للأخص ، من غير عكس فلا تُبْتِدَأُ نبوَّة ولا شريعة بعده (٤) .
وَعَمَّمَا أي: وخُصَّ أيضًا بأنَّ ربَّنا عَمَّم (بِعْثَتْهُ) صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي الزَّمان والمكان ؛ فأرسله إلى جميع المُكلَّفين من الإنس والجن إجماعاً، ويأجوج ومأجوج والملائكة(ه)
وجميع الأنبياء والأمم السابقة(١) ؛ لدخول الجميع تحت قوله : «بعثتُ الساعة ، إلى النَّاس كافَةٌ» (٢) وشُموله لهم مِن لَدُن آدم إلى قيام الساعة
(١) قال العلامة الباجوري في تحفة المريد: والتحقيق أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم مرسل لجميع الأنبياء والأمم السابقة، لكن باعتبار عالم الأرواح، فإن روحه خُلقت قبل الأرواح وأرسلها الله لهم فبلغت الجميع، والأنبياء نوابه في عالم الأجساد ؛ فهو له مرسل لجميع الناس من لدن آدام إلى يوم القيامة حتى إلى نفسه، وإليه الإشارة بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ أَخَذَ اللَّهُ مِيثَقَ النَّبِيِّينَ لَمَا آتَيْتُكُم مِّن كِتَابٍ وَحِكْمَةٍ ثُمَّ جَاءَكُمْ رَسُولٌ مُّصَدِّقٌ لِمَا مَعَكُمْ لَتُؤْمِنُنَّ بِهِ وَلَتَنصُرُنَّهُ قَالَ أَأَقْرَرْتُمْ وَأَخَذْتُمْ عَلَى ذَلِكُمْ إِصْرِى قَالُوا أَقْرَرْنَا قَالَ فَأَشْهَدُوا وَأَنَا مَعَكُم مِّنَ الشَّهِدِينَ) [آل عمران: ٨١] . ونحوه عند الأمير الشنواني .
(٢) رواه مسلم في صحيحه عن أبي هريرة رقم (٥٢٣) ولفظه عنده: (عن أبي هريرة، أنَّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: فضّلْتُ على الأنبياء بست: أُعطيتُ جوامع الكلم، ونُصرت بالرعب، وأُحلَّت لي الغنائم، وجعلت لي الأرض طهورا ومسجدا ، وأُرسلت إلى الخلق كافة، وخُتِم بي النبيون).
His sending to the angels. Without limit or number (1), but the important part is that He has completed all with him. (2) Our Lord — meaning: Our Lord sealed with his prophethood all the prophets, He said: 'And the seal of the prophets' (Quran 33:40). And it follows from that the sealing of the messengers as well, because sealing the more general is sealing the more specific, without the reverse. So no prophethood nor law is initiated after him (4). And 'and He generalized' — meaning: He also specified that our Lord generalized (His mission) may God bless him and grant him peace in time and place; so He sent him to all obligated beings from humans and jinn by consensus, and Gog and Magog and the angels (5). And all the prophets and previous nations (1); because all are included under His saying: 'I was sent at the hour to all people' (2) and its inclusion of them from the time of Adam until the Day of Resurrection. (1) Al-Allama al-Bajuri said in Tuhfat al-Murid: And the verification is that he, may God bless him and grant him peace, is sent to all prophets and previous nations, but in consideration of the world of spirits, for his spirit was created before spirits and God sent it to them and it reached all, and the prophets are his deputies in the world of bodies; so he is sent to all people from Adam until the Day of Resurrection even to himself, and to that points His saying: 'And when God took the covenant of the prophets...' (Quran 3:81). And similar is from al-Amir al-Shanwani. (2) Muslim narrated in his Sahih from Abu Hurayra number (523) and its wording with him: (From Abu Hurayra that the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: I have been favored over the prophets with six: I have been given the comprehensive speech, I have been made victorious with terror, spoils have been made lawful for me, the earth has been made a place of prayer and purification for me, and I have been sent to all creation, and the prophets have been sealed with me).
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage defines the finality of the Prophet's prophethood and the universality of his mission. The author begins by explaining the poem line 'His sending to the angels' as having no limit or count, but the key point is that God completed all prophethood with him. He then explains the word 'our Lord' in the poem: it means God sealed all prophets with Muhammad, citing the Quranic verse 'the seal of the prophets'. From this sealing it necessarily follows that he is also the seal of messengers, because sealing the general category (prophets) entails sealing the specific category (messengers), but not the reverse. Consequently, no new prophethood or law can be initiated after him; this guards against the exception of Jesus, who will return as a follower of Muhammad's law. The passage then explains 'and He generalized': God generalized his mission in time and place, sending him to all obligated beings: humans, jinn by consensus, Gog and Magog, and angels. It adds 'and all the prophets and previous nations' because all are included under the hadith 'I was sent to all people' and its inclusive scope from Adam to the Day of Resurrection. A footnote from al-Bajuri clarifies that in reality, Muhammad is sent to all prophets and nations in the world of spirits, as his spirit was created first and sent to them, and the prophets are his deputies in the physical world. The hadith listing the six special favors confirms the universal mission.

Key Terms
ختم النبوة
عموم البعثة
المرسلين
المكلفين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that finality of prophethood means no other messenger ever, including that Jesus cannot return.
Correction: The passage explains that finality means no new law, and Jesus will return as a follower of Muhammad's law. Additionally, the sealing is of the general category (prophets), which includes messengers, so no new messenger with a new law can come.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the sealing of prophethood necessarily entail the sealing of messengers?
A) Because every messenger is a prophet.
B) Because the Quran explicitly says so.
C) Because sealing the general (prophets) includes the specific (messengers).
D) Because the Prophet said so.

Key Takeaway
Muhammad is the final prophet and messenger, sent to all beings from Adam to the end of time, and no new law will come after him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if Muhammad is the final prophet, or do you sometimes seek guidance from ideologies that contradict or add to his message? What would change if you fully internalized that no new law will come?
?
The Prophet was sent to all beings, including you. Are you actively representing his mission in your daily interactions? What specific step can you take today to embody his message of mercy and truth?

The Re-creation of Time and the Quranic Proof
Sanusi discusses two opinions on re-creation of time and argues for the preferred view using Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the preferred opinion on the re-creation of time in the afterlife and how a Quranic verse is used as evidence.

Core Idea
Time is re-created with bodies; the Quranic verse proves temporal otherness.

Sanusi addresses a subtle question: Are the times of bodies re-created in the afterlife? He presents two opinions and defends the stronger one using a clear Quranic proof. This lesson unpacks his argument and the key concept of 'temporal otherness'.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of time
Read how Sanusi defines time as a known renewal used to measure unknown renewals. Note the example: 'I will come at sunrise'.
2
Identify the two opinions
Find the two opinions about re-creating time. Note which one is deemed preponderant.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Read the verse (4:56) and understand how Sanusi interprets 'other skins' as temporal otherness.
4
Review the additional miracle proof
Note the mention of the sun returning by supplication as further support for re-creating time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
100. وفي الزَّمَنْ قَوْلَانِ والحِسَابُ حَقُّ وَمَا فِي حَقٌّ ارْتِيَابُ (وَفِي) جواز إعادة (الزَّمَنْ هو مُتجدِّدُ معلوم ، يُقدَّر به مُتجدّد غير معلوم، وهو كقولهم: مُقارنة مُتَجَدِّدٍ موهوم لمُتَجَدِّدٍ معلوم ، إزالة للإبهام، نحو: آتيك عند طلوع الشَّمس (قَوْلَانِ): أحدهما: - وهو الأرجح - : إعادة جميع أزمنة الأجسام التي مرَّتْ عليها الدُّنيا تبعاً للذوات والأجسام المُعادَة؛ فَتُعاد بأزمِنَتِها وأوقاتِها كما تُعاد بأَكْوَانِها وهَيْئَاتِها؛ لورودِ ظاهر القرآن به في قوله تعالى: ﴿ كُلَّمَا نَضِجَتْ جُلُودُهُم بَدَّلْتَهُمْ جُلُودًا غَيْرَهَا) [النساء: ٥٦]، لأنَّ المُراد الغيريَّة بحسب الزمان؛ وإلا فالجلود هي الأولى بأعيانها؛ إذ هي التي عَصتْ، فيُعاد تأليفها إذا تفرّقت وأعيانها إذا عُدمت، وقد رُدَّتِ الشَّمسُ بعد غروبها بدعائه.
100. And concerning time there are two opinions, and reckoning is true, and there is no doubt in the truth. Concerning the permissibility of re-creating time—time is a known renewal by which an unknown renewal is measured, and it is like their saying: the correlation of an imagined renewal to a known renewal, to remove ambiguity, such as 'I will come to you at sunrise'—(there are two opinions): One of them—and it is the more preponderant—is: the re-creation of all the times of the bodies that passed in the world, following the re-created selves and bodies; so they are re-created with their times and moments just as they are re-created with their states (akwan) and attributes (hay'at); due to the apparent Quranic proof for it in His saying: 'Whenever their skins are roasted, We will replace them with other skins' (4:56), because the intended otherness is with respect to time; otherwise the skins are the very first ones, for they are the ones that disobeyed, so their composition is re-created when they become disintegrated and their essences when they become non-existent, and the sun was returned after its setting by his supplication.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage presents two opinions on the re-creation of time (zaman) in the afterlife. It first defines time: it is a known renewal (mutajaddid ma'lum) by which unknown renewals are measured, like correlating an imagined renewal to a known one (e.g., 'at sunrise'). The preferred opinion is that all the specific times that elapsed for bodies in this world are re-created along with the bodies and selves themselves. Thus, bodies are re-created with their times and moments, just as they are re-created with their states (akwan: motions, rests) and attributes. This view is supported by the apparent meaning of Quran 4:56, which speaks of replacing skins. The 'otherness' of the skins is interpreted as temporal otherness (different times), not essential otherness; the skins are the very same ones that sinned. The proof also cites the miracle of the sun being returned after sunset by the Prophet's supplication, indicating that times can be re-created.

Key Terms
الزَّمَنْ (time)
إعادة (re-creation)
مُتجدِّد (renewal)
أكوان (states/modes)
هيئات (attributes)
الغيرية (otherness)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Re-created times are entirely new times unconnected to the original.
Correction: The passage argues that the very same times of the bodies are re-created, as part of the bodies' accidents.

Checkpoint
According to the preferred opinion, why are the times of bodies re-created?
A) Because time is an independent substance.
B) Because the Quran explicitly commands re-creation of time.
C) Because the re-creation of bodies necessitates re-creation of their accidents, including time.
D) Because time is eternal and cannot be destroyed.

Key Takeaway
The preferred opinion holds that all the times of bodies are re-created with them, supported by Quranic evidence of temporal otherness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You will be re-created with every moment of your life replayed. Which specific times in your past are you most ashamed of, and what are you doing now to change those moments into repentance before they return?
?
If the skins that sinned are the very same ones that will feel punishment, do you truly believe that your body will witness every deed? What habit do you need to break today because it will be attached to you eternally?
?
The sun was returned by a prophet's du'a. What one prayer can you start making now, knowing that Allah can re-create time itself to answer it?

The Objectivity of Reality
Demonstrates that the reality of every existent is fixed in the external world, independent of mental consideration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Islamic theology affirms that the essences of things are objectively real in the external world, not merely mental constructs.

Core Idea
Reality is not a mind-game; the essences of things are fixed outside our minds.

Sanusi opens his great work by grounding the whole project in realism. Before he can talk about what God is or what we can know, he needs to establish that the world exists independently of our thoughts. This passage does exactly that, affirming that every existent has a fixed reality in the external world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the English translation. Let the author's direct assertion sink in.
Notice the inclusive language 'every existent'.
2
Identify the scope of the predicate
The passage says the reality is fixed for 'every existent, whether necessary or possible'. This includes God (the Necessary Being) and all contingent creatures.
This refutes the idea that only material things are objectively real.
3
Understand the refutation of skepticism
The author emphasizes 'without regard to the consideration of the considerer nor the supposition of the supposer'. This rejects any notion that reality depends on perception.
This is crucial for later arguments about knowledge and attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أنَّ حقيقة كل موجود ثابتة في الخارج والعيان. (وَثَابِتُ في الخَارج خبرُ قوله : (المَوْجُودُ) الواقع مبتدأ، يعني: أنا نقطعُ ونتحقق أنَّ حقيقة كُلَّ موجود ثابتة ومتحققة في الخارج ونفس الأمر، واجبةً كانت أو ممكنةً، من غير نظر إلى اعتبار المعتبر ولا فَرْض الفَارِضِ، فما نعتقده حقائق الأشياء ونسميه بالأسماء من الإنسان والفرس والسَّماء والأرض .. أمور موجودة في نفس الأمر.
A statement that the reality of every existent is fixed in the external world and in clear perception. (And 'fixed in the external world' is the predicate of the word 'the existent' which is the subject. Meaning: We are certain and verified that the reality of every existent is fixed and realized in the external world and in the same thing, whether it be necessary or possible, without regard to the consideration of the considerer nor the supposition of the supposer. So what we consider as the realities of things and name with names such as human, horse, sky, and earth are existing things in the same thing.)
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This passage states the foundational realist position in kalam: the essences (haqa'iq) of things are fixed in the external world (al-kharij) and in the thing itself (nafs al-amr), independent of any mental consideration. It affirms that existence in the mind is not the same as existence in reality; the latter is objective. The author explains that the predicate 'thabit fi al-kharij' (fixed in the external world) applies to every existent, whether necessary (wajib) or contingent (mumkin). He then clarifies that the 'realities' we conceive and name correspond to actual external objects. This refutes skepticism and nominalism by asserting that our concepts are grounded in an objective reality.

Key Terms
حقيقة
موجود
خارج
نفس الأمر
واجب
ممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The predicate 'fixed in the external world' applies only to contingent beings, not to God.
Correction: The text explicitly says 'whether necessary or possible' (واجبةً كانت أو ممكنةً), so it includes God (the Necessary Being) as well.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does the phrase 'fixed in the external world' (ثابت في الخارج) apply to?
A) Only contingent beings
B) Only necessary beings
C) Every existent, whether necessary or contingent
D) Only material objects

Key Takeaway
The reality of every existent, including God, is objectively fixed in the external world and does not depend on mental consideration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as though the reality of Allah is fixed in the external world, or do you sometimes treat His existence as a mental concept you can switch on and off? What would change today if you truly internalized that His reality is as objective as the ground beneath your feet?
?
You name things like 'sky' and 'earth' every day, but do you ever pause to reflect that their realities are fixed independently of your consideration? How does that reframe your relationship with creation and the Creator?
?
If the reality of every existent is fixed and independent of your mental states, then your doubts or negligence do not alter Allah's existence. How does this thought compel you to move from passive belief to active certainty that shapes your actions starting now?

Ash'ari View: Existence Identical to Essence in External Reality
States the Ash'ari position that existence is not added to essence externally.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position that existence is not added to essence in external reality, and its implication that non-existent things have no external reality.

Core Idea
For the Ash'aris, existence and essence are one in the external world — there is no extra 'existence' tag.

This lesson introduces a central Ash'ari doctrine that distinguishes them from other theological schools. The text from Jawharat al-Tawhid states that existence is identical to essence, and the commentary clarifies that what we perceive externally is the essence itself qualified by existence. We will unpack this idea and see its surprising consequence for non-existent things.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Let the author's own words set the stage before analyzing.
Pay attention to the phrase 'وجود شيء عينه'.
2
Understand the key claim: existence = essence externally
The core idea is that existence is not an extra attribute added to essence in external reality. Instead, the existent thing's reality is exactly its existence. This is explained with the analogy of redness in a red object.
Contrast this with the view that existence is an accident added to an already-real essence.
3
Grasp the consequence for non-existent things
If existence and essence are identical externally, then a non-existent thing has no reality at all in the external world. It only becomes a 'thing' when it exists.
This opposes the Mu'tazilite view that non-existent things have some fixed reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخلف في زيادة الوجود على الماهية وعدمه. الفرد حادث عندنا لا ينكر ١٢٢. وجود شيء عينه والجوهر. (وجود شيء عينه) يعني: أن وجود كل شيء (٦) من الموجودات عين حقيقته وليس زائدا على الماهية، بمعنى أنه ليس الخارج والمحسوس إلا الذات المتصفة بالوجود، من غير أن يتحقق فيه ذات معروضة للوجود لها فيه تحقق، ولعارضها المسمى بالوجود وجود آخر، كوجود الذات المتصفة بالحمرة (٧) وعارضها الذي هو الحمرة القائمة بها هذا ما عليه الأشاعرة، وعليه: فالمعدوم ليس في الخارج بشيء ولا ذات ولا ثابت، أي: لا حقيقة له في الخارج، وإنما يتحقق بوجوده فيه (٨).
The dispute about whether existence is additional to essence or not. The individual is originated with us, not denied 122. The existence of a thing is its very essence and the substance. (The existence of a thing is its very essence) means: that the existence of every thing (6) of existing things is identical to its reality and not additional to the essence, meaning that nothing exists in the external and sensible except the essence qualified by existence, without there being realized in it an essence that is a subject of existence having its own realization, and for its accident called existence another existence, like the existence of an essence qualified by redness (7) and its accident which is the redness subsisting in it; this is the position of the Ash'aris. And accordingly: the non-existent is not in the external world a thing, nor an essence, nor a fixed entity, i.e., it has no reality in the external world; rather, it is realized by its existence therein (8).
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage presents the Ash'ari position on the relationship between existence and essence. It begins by restating the heading of the dispute: whether existence is additional to essence or not. Then it quotes the poetic line of Jawharat al-Tawhid: 'The existence of a thing is its very essence and the substance.' The commentary explains: the existence of every existent is identical to its reality, not an added increment. In external reality, what we find is the essence itself qualified by existence, not a separate entity that is the subject of existence with another existence added to it. The analogy of redness is provided: just as a red object's essence is not separate from its redness, similarly existence is not a separate accident in the external world. The passage concludes that non-existent things have no external reality at all; they only become realized when they come into existence.

Key Terms
الوجود
الماهية
عين الماهية
الموجود
المعدوم
الأشاعرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Ash'aris deny any distinction between existence and essence even conceptually.
Correction: They affirm a conceptual (mental) distinction between existence and essence while denying that they are separate in external reality. In the mind, we can consider essence without existence, but in the world, they are identical.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'aris, what is the relationship between a thing's existence and its essence?
A) Existence is an added attribute separate from essence.
B) Existence is identical to essence in external reality.
C) Existence is a mental concept with no external reality.
D) Essence is prior to existence in the world.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'aris hold that existence is not an extra attribute added to essence in external reality; it is the essence itself qualified by existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If existence and essence are one in external reality, how does that challenge the way you sometimes distinguish between 'just existing' and 'being yourself'? In what specific areas of your life do you need to stop treating your existence as a mere add-on and instead embrace it as fully identical to who you are?
?
The passage says non-existent things have no reality at all. Consider a goal or a change you desire in your life: in what ways are you acting as if it already has reality before God grants it existence? What would it mean for you to truly rely on Him to bring it into being?
?
The analogy of redness shows that an accident is not separate from the essence. Think of your own deeds: are they temporary additions to your identity, or are they the very realization of your self before Allah? How would your accountability change if you saw your actions as directly constituting your essence?

The Indivisible Atom: Definition and Contingency Proof
Defines al-jawhar al-fard and argues for its contingency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) in kalam, its distinction from God and accidents, its absolute indivisibility, and the proof of its contingency from the world's contingency.

Core Idea
The indivisible atom is the fundamental building block of all bodies, indivisible by any means, and proven contingent from the world's contingency.

This lesson introduces one of the key concepts of kalam cosmology: the indivisible atom. The author defines what it means for a substance to be 'indivisible' and explains why this notion is fundamental to understanding the contingent nature of the physical world. By studying this passage, you will see how the mutakallimūn argued for the existence of atomic particles and used them as a basis for proving the world's creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage slowly, then its literal translation. Notice the dense style and the key terms.
Pay attention to the parentheses indicating earlier and later terminologies.
2
Understand the definition of al-jawhar and al-fard
Identify the two definitions: the general meaning of substance (occupying space essentially) and the specific meaning of 'fard' (absolute indivisibility).
3
Note what is excluded: Allah and accidents
The passage explicitly excludes the Necessary Existent (God) because He does not occupy space, and accidents because they depend on a locus. This clarifies the boundaries of the definition.
This distinction is crucial for kalam arguments about the contingent world.
4
Examine the proof of contingency and the conclusion
The proof is simple: the atom is part of the world, and the world's contingency is already established. The passage ends by affirming that all bodies are composed of finite atoms, rejecting the philosophers' denial.
Notice the phrase 'according to us it is not denied'—this underscores the conviction of the mutakallimūn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ذكر مسألة أخرى مما ينفع علمه ولا يضر جهله، وهي إثبات الجوهر الفرد وحدوثه، فقال: (والجوهر الفرد هذه عبارة المتقدمين، وعبر المتأخرون بدلها بـ: الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ). والجوهر: ما يشغل الحيز، وهو عند المتكلمين: الموجود المتحيز بالذات، أعني ما يتحيز غير تابع في تحيزه لغيره؛ فخرج الواجب الوجود لانتفاء التحيز عنه، وخرج العرض لتبعيته في التحيز لمحله. والمراد من وصفه بالفرد: أن لا يقبل الانقسام أصلا، لا قطعا ولا كسرا، ولا وهما ولا فرضا. وقوله: (حادت) خبر الجوهر الواقع مبتدأ، أي: ثابت مسبوق وجوده بالعدم؛ لما تقدم من أدلة حدوث العالم وكل جزء من أجزائه التي منها الجوهر الفرد، ولا معنى للحادث إلا ما كان مسبوقا بالعدم، أي: لم يكن ثم كان. (عندنا لا ينكر) ثبوته وتقرره في الوجود، فجميع الأجسام تركبت منه مع تناهي آحاده فيها، خلافا لحكماء الفلاسفة.
Then he mentioned another issue, the knowledge of which is beneficial and ignorance of it is not harmful, namely: establishing the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) and its contingency. He said: (The indivisible atom—this is the expression of the earlier scholars; the later scholars replaced it with 'the part which does not divide further'). Al-jawhar (substance) is that which occupies space, and according to the mutakallimūn: an existent that is essentially spatial, i.e., that occupies space without being dependent in its occupancy on another. So the Necessary Existent (al-wājib al-wujūd) is excluded because occupancy does not apply to Him, and accidents (al-aʿrāḍ) are excluded because they are dependent in occupancy on their locus. What is meant by describing it as 'indivisible' (al-fard) is that it does not accept division at all, neither by cutting nor by breaking, nor by imagination nor by supposition. And His saying: 'contingent' (ḥādiṯ) is the predicate of 'jawhar' which is the subject, meaning: its existence is preceded by non-existence, due to what has preceded from the proofs of the contingency of the world and every part of its parts among which is the indivisible atom. There is no meaning to 'contingent' except that which is preceded by non-existence, i.e., it was not then it was. (According to us it is not denied) its establishment and confirmation in existence, so all bodies are composed of it, with its units being finite in them, contrary to the philosophers.
Source pages p. 584

Commentary
This passage defines the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) and provides proof of its contingency. It begins by identifying the issue as beneficial to know, then presents the definition of al-jawhar as that which occupies space essentially, distinguishing it from God (who does not occupy space) and accidents (which are dependent). The term 'fard' indicates absolute indivisibility: the atom cannot be divided physically, mentally, or by supposition. The proof of contingency (ḥudūth) is that the atom is part of the world, and the world's contingency has already been established; thus the atom is preceded by non-existence. The passage concludes by affirming that all bodies are composed of finite atoms, rejecting the philosophers' denial of the indivisible atom.

Key Terms
الجوهر الفرد
الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ
الحادث
المتحيز
العرض
الواجب الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the indivisible atom is a physical particle that can be divided by imagination or science.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that the atom does not accept division at all, neither by cutting, breaking, imagination, nor supposition. It is a conceptual indivisible unit, not a physical particle.

Checkpoint
What does the passage state about the indivisible atom's relationship to bodies?
A) Bodies are not composed of atoms.
B) Bodies are composed of finite indivisible atoms.
C) Bodies are composed of infinite indivisible atoms.
D) Bodies are composed of atoms only according to philosophers.

Key Takeaway
The indivisible atom is a fundamental substance that is essentially spatial, indivisible, and contingent; all bodies are composed of finite such atoms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every atom in your body was non-existent and then brought into existence by Allah, what claim do you have to independence? In what area of your life today are you living as if you are self-sufficient?
?
The scholars said knowledge of the indivisible atom is beneficial but ignorance is not harmful. Yet you have just learned it. What does this tell you about the depth of Islamic theology? Will you let this knowledge increase your awe of Allah, or will you treat it as abstract information?
?
The philosophers denied the indivisible atom because it contradicted their worldview. Are there any beliefs you hold that contradict what the Quran and Sunnah teach? Are you willing to submit your intellect to revelation, even when it challenges modern assumptions?

The Indivisible Atom and Its Contingency
Defines the indivisible atom and its contingency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) as a temporally originated substance, and how its contingency is established based on earlier proofs of the world's temporality.

Core Idea
The indivisible atom is a created entity, its existence preceded by non-existence.

In this passage, the commentator explains a key term in kalam cosmology: the indivisible atom. Building on earlier arguments for the temporality of the world, he defines the atom as a temporally originated substance (ḥādith) and asserts that all bodies are composed of such finite atoms. This stands in contrast to the philosophers who deny the atom's existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the grammatical structure: 'ḥādit' is the predicate of 'al-jawhar'.
2
Understand the definition of ḥādith
The author defines ḥādith as 'what is preceded by non-existence'. This is a precise technical term meaning something that came into being after not existing.
Contrast it with qadīm (eternal).
3
See the basis in earlier proofs
The passage refers to 'what has preceded of proofs of the temporality of the world'. The atom is part of the world, so it too is contingent.
4
Learn the composition of bodies
All bodies are said to be composed of these indivisible atoms, and the atoms are finite in number within a body. This is the Ashʿarī view.
Opposed by the philosophers (falāsifa) who deny the atom.
5
Reflect on the opposition
Consider why the philosophers might reject the indivisible atom. The commentary will help you understand the stance of kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله: (حَادِتْ) خبر الجوهر الواقع مبتدأ، أي: ثابت مسبوق وجوده بالعدم؛ لما تقدَّم مِن أدلة حدوث العالم وكل جزء من أجزائه التي منها الجوهر الفرد، ولا معنى للحادث إلا ما كان مسبوقاً بالعدم، أي: لم يكن ثُمَّ كانَ، (عِنْدَنَا لَا يُنْكَرُ) ثبوتُه وتَقرُّرُه في الوجود، فجميع الأجسام تركبت منه مع تناهي آحاده فيها، خلافا لحكماء الفلاسفة.
And His saying: (ʿādhītu) is the predicate of al-jawhar (the substance) which is the subject, meaning: established, its existence preceded by non-existence; due to what has preceded of proofs of the temporality of the world and every part of its parts, among which is al-jawhar al-fard (the indivisible atom). And there is no meaning for al-ḥādith (the temporally originated) except what is preceded by non-existence, i.e., it was not then it was. (ʿindanā lā yunkaru) its being established and determined in existence, so all bodies are composed of it while its individuals are finite in them, contrary to the philosophers.
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage defines the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) and establishes its contingency (ḥudūth). The author explains that the word 'ḥādit' (temporally originated) is the predicate of the subject 'al-jawhar' (the substance), meaning that the atom is a thing whose existence is preceded by non-existence. This is based on the earlier proofs of the temporality of the world and every part of it, including the atom. The phrase 'contemporary entity' (al-ḥādith) is defined precisely: something that was not, and then came to be. Then the author asserts that its existence and determination are not denied by us (the mutakallimūn). The consequence is that all bodies are composed of these indivisible atoms, and the atoms are finite in number within each body. This position is maintained in opposition to the philosophers (falāsifa) who deny the indivisible atom.

Key Terms
الجوهر الفرد
الحادث
العدم
تناهي الآحاد
حكماء الفلاسفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The indivisible atom is the same as the modern physical atom.
Correction: In kalam, al-jawhar al-fard is a metaphysical indivisible substance, argued from logical and theological premises, not from empirical science. It is not a physical particle like the modern atom.

Checkpoint
What does 'ḥādit' (حادث) mean according to the passage?
A) Something that exists eternally
B) Something whose existence is preceded by non-existence
C) Something that is indivisible
D) Something that is composed of other parts

Key Takeaway
The indivisible atom is a contingent substance, composed of finite units that make up all bodies, in contrast to the philosophers' denial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You exist now, but you were nothing before. How does this undeniable contingency reshape your daily reliance on your own existence? Are you living with the awareness that at any moment you could return to non-existence? What one action today will you take to remind yourself that your being is a gift from the One who brought you from non-existence?
?
Everything around you—including your own body—is made of finite, temporal atoms. If every part of your existence is limited and temporary, what part of your life are you treating as if it will last forever? What attachment do you need to break today because it falsely promises permanence?
?
Are there aspects of Islamic doctrine that you accept only because they are intellectually satisfying, rather than because they humble you before Allah? The mutakallimun defended even the smallest particle to affirm Tawhid. What 'small particle' of your faith are you neglecting that could strengthen your conviction?

Forgiveness of Major Sins by Divine Grace
Al-Shanwani clarifies that forgiveness is not exclusively dependent on tawbah; divine grace suffices.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's forgiveness of major sins is not contingent upon repentance; He may forgive by pure grace.

Core Idea
Allah's forgiveness is not bound by tawbah; His grace supersedes.

This lesson clarifies a key Ashʿarī point: tawbah is not a necessary condition for forgiveness. Al-Shanwani explains that major sins can be forgiven by pure divine grace (al-faḍl al-maḥḍ) and lightened by obedience. A hadith reinforces that Allah may cause the recording angels to forget sins upon repentance, but repentance itself is not exclusive.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's exact wording.
Notice the negation 'ليس في كلام المصنف ما يفيد توقف الغفران على التوبة'.
2
Identify the main claim
The author asserts that nothing in his previous speech implies dependence on tawbah. Find the direct statement about forgiveness by pure grace.
The phrase 'فقد تغفر بالفضل المحض' is key.
3
Understand the two categories
The passage presents two ways sins are dealt with: forgiveness by pure grace, and lightening by acts of obedience. See how these are distinct.
The second category uses 'يخفف منها بالطاعات'.
4
Reflect on the hadith
Read the hadith: when a servant repents, Allah makes the guardians forget sins. Consider how this supports the author's point without making tawbah a condition for all forgiveness.
The hadith shows erasure through repentance, but the author says forgiveness can also happen without it.
5
Connect to the core idea
Synthesize: Allah's forgiveness is an act of His will and grace, not mechanically tied to human actions. This upholds divine sovereignty.
This lesson guards against the misconception that repentance is the only path to forgiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس في كلام المصنف رحمه الله تعالى ما يفيد توقفَ غُفران الكبائر على التّوبة ؛ فقد تُغفّر بالفضل المحض ، وقد يُخفَّفُ منها بالطَّاعات ، وفي حديث أنس قال: قال رسول الله صلى عليه وسلَّم: «إذا تَابَ العبدُ أَنْسَى اللَّهُ الحفظة ذُنوبَهُ» خرَّجه ابن عساکر .
And there is nothing in the speech of the author — may Allah have mercy on him — that indicates that the forgiveness of major sins depends on repentance; rather, they may be forgiven by pure grace, and they may be lightened by acts of obedience. And in the hadith of Anas, he said: The Messenger of Allah — may Allah bless him and grant him peace — said: 'When a servant repents, Allah makes the guardians forget his sins.' It was narrated by Ibn 'Asakir.
Source pages p. 592

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential misunderstanding that tawbah is a necessary condition for forgiveness. The author disclaims that his previous statements on tawbah imply that forgiveness is exclusively tied to it. Instead, he affirms that Allah may forgive major sins by pure grace (al-faḍl al-maḥḍ) without any precondition, and that He may lighten the burden of sins through acts of obedience (al-ṭā‘āt). He supports this with a hadith: when a servant repents, Allah causes the recording angels to forget the sins, implying erasure. This reinforces the Ash‘ari doctrine that Allah’s forgiveness is not constrained by human actions; He may forgive by His sheer bounty.

Key Terms
الفضل المحض
الطاعات
غفران
الحفظة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think tawbah is the only path to forgiveness.
Correction: The text shows that Allah may forgive major sins by pure grace, without tawbah.

Checkpoint

B) Forgiveness can also occur by pure grace
C) Forgiveness only occurs through good deeds
D) Forgiveness requires specific supplication

Key Takeaway
Allah may forgive major sins purely by His grace, without requiring repentance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a sin you have committed that you feel is too great to be forgiven. Does this lesson's affirmation of forgiveness by pure grace change how you view that sin? What would it look like for you to truly accept that Allah can forgive it without your having to earn that forgiveness?
?
When you sin, do you rush to repent out of fear that forgiveness is only available through tawbah? How would your relationship with Allah change if you internalized that His mercy is not conditional on your actions, but is an expression of His sheer bounty?
?
If Allah forgives by pure grace, does that make repentance less urgent in your life? Or does it free you to repent out of love rather than fear? Examine your current motivation for tawbah — is it rooted in dread or in gratitude?

The Author's Hope and the World's Origin and Maker's Eternity
Author's hope and first two creedal statements about the world and God

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's aspiration for sincerity and the first foundational creed of Ahl al-Sunnah: that the world is originated and the Maker is eternal with eternal attributes.

Core Idea
The world is not eternal; only the Creator is.

The author begins by expressing his hope for sincerity and then immediately establishes the core Sunni principle: the universe is not eternal but created, and God is eternal with attributes distinct from His essence. This sets the stage for all subsequent theological claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's hope
Read the opening line where the author asks for sincerity and deliverance from hypocrisy. This sets the tone of the work.
Notice the humility of the author.
2
Identify the first two beliefs
The passage states: 'that the world is originated, and the Maker is eternal, described with eternal attributes'. Understand the meaning of hadith (originated) and qadim (eternal).
These are the foundational categories.
3
Define the attributes as neither identical nor other
The attributes are eternal, neither God's essence nor separate. This is the Ash'ari middle ground.
This refutes both annihilation of attributes and multiplicity.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask: Why is it important to affirm that the world is originated? Because it leads to the proof of a Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رجاءُ المُصنفِ تَصحيحَ نيَّتِه وذكرُ عقائدِ أهلِ السُّنَّة الواجبة الاعتقادِ إجمالاً] ١٤٠ هَذَا وَأَرْجُو اللَّهَ فِي الإِخْلَاصِ مِنَ الرِّياءِ ثُمَّ فِي الخَلَاصِ (هذا) الذي ذكرتُه في هذه المنظومة من المتَّفق عليه بين أهل السُّنَّة العقائد: أنَّ العالم حادث ، والصَّانع قديم، متّصف بصفات قديمة، ليست عينه ولا غيره، واحد لا شبيه له ، ولا ضدَّ ولا نِدَّ ولا نهاية له ، ولا صورة ولا حدَّ، ولا يَحُلُّ في شيء، ولا يقوم به حادث ، ولا تصح عليه الحركة والانتقال ، ولا الجهل ولا الكذب ولا النقص، وأنَّه يُرى فى الآخرة ، وليس في حيّز وجهة ، ما شاءَ كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن، ولا يحتاج إلى شيء، ولا يجب عليه شيءٌ ، كلُّ أعمال المخلوقات بقضائه وقدره وإرادته ومشيئته
[The author's hope for correcting his intention and a summary of the beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah that must be held in general] Verse 140: This, and I hope for Allah sincerity from hypocrisy, then deliverance. (This) which I have mentioned in this poem is the agreed-upon beliefs among Ahl al-Sunnah: that the world is originated (ḥādith), and the Maker (al-Ṣāniʿ) is eternal (qadīm), described with eternal attributes (ṣifāt qadīma), neither identical to Him nor other than Him; One with no likeness, no opposite, no rival, no end; no form, no limit; He does not indwell anything, nor does any originated thing subsist in Him; movement and transference are not valid for Him, nor ignorance, falsehood, or deficiency; and that He will be seen in the Hereafter, yet He is not in a spatial direction; what He wills is, and what He does not will is not; He does not need anything, nothing is obligatory upon Him; all the actions of creatures are by His decree, predestination, will, and volition.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage presents the author's hope for sincerity and deliverance, followed by a concise summary of the fundamental beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah (the Sunni creed). The author states that what he has set forth in his poem is the agreed-upon creed. He then lists these beliefs in a continuous chain: (1) The world (al-ʿālam) is originated (ḥādith) — having come into existence after non-existence. (2) The Maker (al-Ṣāniʿ) is eternal (qadīm), and that He has eternal attributes (ṣifāt qadīma) which are neither identical to His essence nor other than it — this is the Ashʿarī position. (3) He is one, with no likeness, opposite (ḍidd), rival (nidd), or end – negating anthropomorphism and multiplicity. (4) He has no form (ṣūra) or limit (ḥadd). (5) He does not indwell anything nor does any originated thing inhere in Him – refuting incarnation and pantheism. (6) Movement, transference, ignorance, falsehood, and deficiency are not possible for Him – affirming divine perfection. (7) He will be seen in the Hereafter (ru’yat Allāh), but not in a direction (jihat). (8) His will is absolute – what He wills occurs, what He does not will does not occur. (9) He does not need anything, nor is anything obligatory upon Him. (10) All actions of creatures are by His decree (qaḍā’), predestination (qadar), will (irāda), and volition (mashī’a) – affirming predestination. This passage serves as a doctrinal summary encapsulating the core tenets of Sunni theology.

Key Terms
عقائد أهل السنة
حادث
قديم
صفات قديمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the world is eternal or that God's attributes are either identical with His essence or separate entities.
Correction: The passage affirms the middle position: the attributes are eternal, neither identical to God nor other, preserving unity and perfection.

?
The attributes of God are neither identical to His essence nor other than Him. This means God's mercy, power, and knowledge are real and belong to Him. Divine Oneness and Transcendence: Negating All Imperfections
Negations of divine likeness, limitation, and defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Sunni creed affirms God's oneness by negating all forms of likeness, limitation, incarnation, and defect.

Core Idea
God is unlike anything, without form, limit, or direction.

After establishing the Creator's eternity, the creed proceeds to negate everything that might imply imperfection or creaturely limitations. This lesson covers the affirmations of God's absolute uniqueness, freedom from indwelling, and perfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of negations
Read carefully: 'One with no likeness, no opposite, no rival, no end; no form, no limit; He does not indwell anything, nor does any originated thing subsist in Him.'
Each negation serves a purpose.
2
Understand the terms
For each term (like shabih, didd, nidd, nihaya), grasp its meaning. 'No opposite' means no equal or counterpart; 'no rival' means no competitor.
These refute polytheism and dualism.
3
Analyze the refutation of incarnation
The statement that God does not indwell anything (hall) and nothing subsist in Him (qiyam) refutes beliefs like anthropomorphism or pantheism.
This is a crucial guard against assimilation (tashbih).
4
Consider the negations of defects
God is not subject to movement, transference, ignorance, falsehood, or deficiency. This affirms divine perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
