Seeing Allah and Absolute Predestination
Doctrines of beatific vision, divine will, and predestination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the beatific vision of Allah in the hereafter and the absolute scope of divine will and predestination.

Core Idea
Allah will be seen, yet He is not in a place; His will is absolute over all actions.

The creed concludes with two essential doctrines: the vision of Allah (ru'ya) in the afterlife, which is possible without spatial location, and the all-encompassing divine decree (qada wa qadar). These affirm both God's transcendence and His complete control over creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the statements on ru'ya
Read: 'He will be seen in the Hereafter, yet He is not in a direction'. This affirms the possibility of seeing God without Him being confined to a place.
This is a distinctive Sunni belief against those who deny vision or claim it requires location.
2
Understand the will and power of Allah
Note: 'what He wills is, and what He does not will is not'. This indicates absolute sovereignty.
This refutes free will without divine decree.
3
Analyze the statement about actions of creatures
All actions of creatures are by His decree, predestination, will, and volition. This affirms predestination.
This does not negate human responsibility; rather, it ties everything to God's power.
4
Reflect on God's self-sufficiency
He does not need anything, and nothing is obligatory upon Him. This underscores His independence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رجاءُ المُصنفِ تَصحيحَ نيَّتِه وذكرُ عقائدِ أهلِ السُّنَّة الواجبة الاعتقادِ إجمالاً] ١٤٠ هَذَا وَأَرْجُو اللَّهَ فِي الإِخْلَاصِ مِنَ الرِّياءِ ثُمَّ فِي الخَلَاصِ (هذا) الذي ذكرتُه في هذه المنظومة من المتَّفق عليه بين أهل السُّنَّة العقائد: أنَّ العالم حادث ، والصَّانع قديم، متّصف بصفات قديمة، ليست عينه ولا غيره، واحد لا شبيه له ، ولا ضدَّ ولا نِدَّ ولا نهاية له ، ولا صورة ولا حدَّ، ولا يَحُلُّ في شيء، ولا يقوم به حادث ، ولا تصح عليه الحركة والانتقال ، ولا الجهل ولا الكذب ولا النقص، وأنَّه يُرى فى الآخرة ، وليس في حيّز وجهة ، ما شاءَ كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن، ولا يحتاج إلى شيء، ولا يجب عليه شيءٌ ، كلُّ أعمال المخلوقات بقضائه وقدره وإرادته ومشيئته
[The author's hope for correcting his intention and a summary of the beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah that must be held in general] Verse 140: This, and I hope for Allah sincerity from hypocrisy, then deliverance. (This) which I have mentioned in this poem is the agreed-upon beliefs among Ahl al-Sunnah: that the world is originated (ḥādith), and the Maker (al-Ṣāniʿ) is eternal (qadīm), described with eternal attributes (ṣifāt qadīma), neither identical to Him nor other than Him; One with no likeness, no opposite, no rival, no end; no form, no limit; He does not indwell anything, nor does any originated thing subsist in Him; movement and transference are not valid for Him, nor ignorance, falsehood, or deficiency; and that He will be seen in the Hereafter, yet He is not in a spatial direction; what He wills is, and what He does not will is not; He does not need anything, nothing is obligatory upon Him; all the actions of creatures are by His decree, predestination, will, and volition.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage presents the author's hope for sincerity and deliverance, followed by a concise summary of the fundamental beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah (the Sunni creed). The author states that what he has set forth in his poem is the agreed-upon creed. He then lists these beliefs in a continuous chain: (1) The world (al-ʿālam) is originated (ḥādith) — having come into existence after non-existence. (2) The Maker (al-Ṣāniʿ) is eternal (qadīm), and that He has eternal attributes (ṣifāt qadīma) which are neither identical to His essence nor other than it — this is the Ashʿarī position. (3) He is one, with no likeness, opposite (ḍidd), rival (nidd), or end – negating anthropomorphism and multiplicity. (4) He has no form (ṣūra) or limit (ḥadd). (5) He does not indwell anything nor does any originated thing inhere in Him – refuting incarnation and pantheism. (6) Movement, transference, ignorance, falsehood, and deficiency are not possible for Him – affirming divine perfection. (7) He will be seen in the Hereafter (ru’yat Allāh), but not in a direction (jihat). (8) His will is absolute – what He wills occurs, what He does not will does not occur. (9) He does not need anything, nor is anything obligatory upon Him. (10) All actions of creatures are by His decree (qaḍā’), predestination (qadar), will (irāda), and volition (mashī’a) – affirming predestination. This passage serves as a doctrinal summary encapsulating the core tenets of Sunni theology.

الآخرة
حيّز
جهة
ما شاء كان
قضاء
قدر
إرادة
مشيئة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that predestination negates human responsibility or that seeing God implies God is material.
Correction: The passage affirms predestination while also teaching that God will be seen in a manner befitting His transcendence, not as a physical object.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, will the believers see Allah in the Hereafter?
A) Yes, but only in a direction
B) Yes, without being in a direction
C) No, He is invisible
D) Yes, but only with physical eyes

Key Takeaway
Allah will be seen in paradise yet He is not in space; His will is absolute over all things.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If everything that happens is by Allah's will, why do you still resist what He has decreed for you? Is there an area of your life where you are not content with His plan, and what would it take for you to surrender to it?
?
Knowing that you will see Allah in the Hereafter, how does that reality influence what you do right now? What would change in your daily priorities if you truly lived with the certainty of that vision?
?
The passage says nothing is obligatory upon Allah. What does that mean for how you approach Him in worship—do you approach Him as one who is owed something, or as one who is entirely dependent on His mercy?

The World is Created, the Maker is Eternal
Sanusi introduces the first two agreed-upon beliefs: the world's creation and the Creator's eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the temporality of the world and the eternity of the Creator are the first two agreed-upon beliefs of Ahl al-Sunna.

Core Idea
Everything that begins exists depends on an eternal Creator.

Sanusi begins his creed by stating two foundational beliefs that establish the relationship between creation and Creator. These are not arbitrary but logically necessary. In this lesson, we examine these two pillars of Sunni theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Focus on the Arabic phrases 'عالم حادث' and 'صانع قديم'. Notice the contrast between temporal and eternal.
2
Understand the logical priority
Why is it important to state the world's temporality before the Creator's eternity? Consider that if the world were eternal, it would not need a Creator.
3
Connect to daily aqeedah
These two beliefs are the foundation for all other attributes of Allah. Memorize them as the starting point of your creed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هَذَا وَأَرْجُو اللَّهَ فِي الإِخْلَاصِ مِنَ الرِّياءِ ثُمَّ فِي الخَلَاصِ من (هذا) الذي ذكرتُه في هذه المنظومة من المتَّفق عليه بين أهل السُّنَّة العقائد: أنَّ العالم حادث، والصَّانع قديم، متّصف بصفات قديمة، ليست عينه ولا غيره، واحد لا شبيه له، ولا ضدَّ ولا نِدَّ ولا نهاية له، ولا صورة ولا حدَّ، ولا يَحُلُّ في شيء، ولا يقوم به حادث، ولا تصح عليه الحركة والانتقال، ولا الجهل ولا الكذب ولا النقص، وأنَّه يُرى فى الآخرة، وليس في حيّز وجهة، ما شاءَ كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن، ولا يحتاج إلى شيء، ولا يجب عليه شيءٌ، كلُّ أعمال المخلوقات بقضائه وقدره وإرادته ومشيئته، لكنَّ القبائح منها ليست برضَاهُ وأمرِهِ ومحبّتِهِ .
This – and I ask Allah for sincerity and freedom from hypocrisy, then for salvation – from what I have mentioned in this poem of the agreed-upon beliefs of Ahl al-Sunna: that the world is created, and the Maker is eternal, described with eternal attributes, which are neither His essence nor other than it, one with no likeness, no adversary, no equal, no end, no form, no limit; He does not dwell in anything, nor does any originated thing dwell in Him; movement and transference are not valid for Him; nor ignorance, lying, or deficiency; and that He will be seen in the hereafter, not in a place or direction; whatever He wills is, and whatever He does not will is not; He is not in need of anything, and nothing is obligatory upon Him; all actions of creatures are by His decree, power, will, and volition, but evil actions are not with His pleasure, command, and love.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of core Sunni beliefs about Allah. It begins with a poetic line expressing hope for sincerity, then lists the agreed-upon doctrines. First, the world is temporal (hadith) and the Maker eternal (qadim). The attributes are eternal (qadima), neither identical to the essence nor other than it — a key Ash'ari formulation. Then it negates anthropomorphism: no likeness, adversary, equal, end, form, limit. It negates indwelling (hulul) and originated events inhering in Him. It negates movement, ignorance, etc. It affirms the vision of Allah (ru'ya) in the afterlife without spatiality. It affirms absolute will and power: whatever He wills, is; whatever He does not will, is not. Nothing is obligatory upon Him. Finally, it affirmsthat all actions of creatures are by His decree and will, but evil actions are not with His pleasure, command, or love — a distinction to avoid attributing evil to Him in an approving sense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the world is eternal or that Allah is temporal.
Correction: The passage affirms the opposite: the world is temporal, Allah is eternal.

Checkpoint

A) Eternal
B) Created

The two foundational beliefs of Ahl al-Sunna are that the world is created and the Creator is eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just affirmed that the world is created (ḥādith). Do you truly live each moment aware that your entire existence—your breath, your health, your intellect—was brought into being from nothing and is sustained only by the Eternal Maker? What would change in your daily routine if you genuinely believed that?
?
The source calls Allah 'al-Ṣāniʿ', the Maker. Does your heart rest in the fact that He is eternal (qadīm), or do you sometimes seek security in created, perishing things? Name one created thing you rely on excessively and decide today to shift that reliance to the Eternal Maker.
?
Are you content with being merely a created being, or do you resent your dependence? Confront the pride within you that wants to be self-sufficient. How will you consciously acknowledge, before you sleep tonight, that your life is entirely in the hands of the One who has no beginning?

Divine Attributes: Eternal, Neither Essence Nor Other
Sanusi defines the nature of divine attributes as eternal and distinct from the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position that Allah's attributes are eternal, distinct from His essence yet not separate from it.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are real and eternal, but not identical to His essence nor other than it.

After establishing the Creator's eternity, Sanusi clarifies the nature of His attributes. This is a crucial point in Ash'ari theology that avoids both anthropomorphism and stripping Allah of His attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic phrase
Note 'متّصف بصفات قديمة' (described with eternal attributes) and 'ليست عينه ولا غيره' (neither His essence nor other).
2
Understand the via media
This formulation rejects two extremes: that attributes are identical to the essence (which would imply they are not real) and that they are fully other (which would imply plurality in God).
3
See the connection to earlier lesson
The attributes are eternal (qadīma) just like the Maker is eternal (qadīm). They are not created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If Allah's attributes are neither His essence nor other than it, then His mercy, justice, and power are truly His and not detached concepts. How does this reality make your worship more intimate today?
?

Negations of Anthropomorphism: No Likeness, Adversary, End, Form, Limit
Sanusi negates anthropomorphic attributes from Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key negations that protect Allah from any resemblance to creation.

Core Idea
Allah is unique — no likeness, no adversary, no end, no form, no limit.

The creed continues by negating any possible similarity between Allah and created beings. This establishes tanzih (transcendence). Each negation eliminates a potential misunderstanding.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of negations
Notice the sequence: no likeness (shabīh), no adversary (ḍidd), no equal (nidd), no end (nihāya), no form (ṣūra), no limit (ḥadd).
2
Understand each term
'No end' means not finite; 'no form' means not a body; 'no limit' means no boundaries. Together they rule out any spatial or corporeal attributes.
3
Reflect on why these are necessary
If Allah had any of these, He would be bounded or comparable, contradicting His perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Negations of Change: No Indwelling, No Originated Events, No Movement
Sanusi negates indwelling, movement, and deficiency from Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah is not subject to change or location.

Core Idea
Allah does not dwell in anything, nor does anything dwell in Him, and He is free from movement and deficiency.

The creed now addresses potential misconceptions about Allah's relationship with the world. Sanusi denies that Allah indwells creation (hulul) or that creation indwells Him. This refutes pantheistic ideas.

Guided Path
1
Read the negations
Note 'لا يحُلُّ في شيء ولا يقوم به حادث' (He does not dwell in anything, nor does any originated thing dwell in Him) and 'لا تصح عليه الحركة والانتقال' (movement and transference are not valid for Him).
2
Understand the implications
Dwelling implies spatial containment, which is impossible for Allah. Originated events in Him would imply change, which contradicts His perfection.
3
Connect to other attributes
The denial of movement, ignorance, lying, and deficiency shows Allah's absolute perfection and transcendence over change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some say that Allah 'descends' or 'moves' in a literal sense.
Correction: The passage negates movement and transference from Allah. Such terms are metaphorical.

Checkpoint
What does 'la yaqumu bihi hadith' mean?
A) Allah does not dwell in anything
B) No temporal event occurs in Allah
C) Allah does not move
D) Allah does not lie

Key Takeaway
Allah is free from all change, location, and imperfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson negates indwelling. Do you ever feel that Allah is far from you because you cannot see Him physically? How does this truth that He is not contained in any place actually bring you closer to Him? What will you do today to live with the awareness that He is with you by His knowledge and presence, even without physical nearness?
?
Allah is free from ignorance. He knows every secret of your heart. Does that knowledge fill you with awe or fear? What is one thought or habit you would change right now if you truly believed that Allah's knowledge demands accountability?
?
Allah is without deficiency. How often do you project human limitations onto Allah, expecting Him to fail you or be partial? How does this lesson challenge your trust in Him? Commit to one specific act today that shows you rely on His perfection, not your own.

Allah's Existence
intermediate
5 min
Vision of Allah and Absolute Will
Sanusi affirms the beatific vision and the absolute sovereignty of Allah's will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni belief that Allah will be seen in the afterlife and that His will is absolute.

Core Idea
Allah will be seen by the believers in Paradise, and His will is unbounded.

After the negations, Sanusi affirms two important positive beliefs: the vision of Allah (ru'ya) in the hereafter and the absolute nature of His will and independence.

Guided Path
1
Read the affirmations
Note 'يُرى فى الآخرة' (He will be seen in the hereafter) and 'ما شاءَ كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن' (whatever He wills is, and whatever He does not will is not).
2
Understand the vision
This vision is not with physical eyes as we know, but it is a real seeing, without spatiality.
3
Understand absolute will
Nothing constrains Allah's will; what He wills occurs, what He does not will does not occur.
4
Note the negation of need
He does not need anything, nor is anything obligatory upon Him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هَذَا وَأَرْجُو اللَّهَ فِي الإِخْلَاصِ مِنَ الرِّياءِ ثُمَّ فِي الخَلَاصِ من (هذا) الذي ذكرتُه في هذه المنظومة من المتَّفق عليه بين أهل السُّنَّة العقائد: أنَّ العالم حادث، والصَّانع قديم، متّصف بصفات قديمة، ليست عينه ولا غيره، واحد لا شبيه له، ولا ضدَّ ولا نِدَّ ولا نهاية له، ولا صورة ولا حدَّ، ولا يَحُلُّ في شيء، ولا يقوم به حادث، ولا تصح عليه الحركة والانتقال، ولا الجهل ولا الكذب ولا النقص، وأنَّه يُرى فى الآخرة، وليس في حيّز وجهة، ما شاءَ كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن، ولا يحتاج إلى شيء، ولا يجب عليه شيءٌ، كلُّ أعمال المخلوقات بقضائه وقدره وإرادته ومشيئته، لكنَّ القبائح منها ليست برضَاهُ وأمرِهِ ومحبّتِهِ .
This – and I ask Allah for sincerity and freedom from hypocrisy, then for salvation – from what I have mentioned in this poem of the agreed-upon beliefs of Ahl al-Sunna: that the world is created, and the Maker is eternal, described with eternal attributes, which are neither His essence nor other than it, one with no likeness, no adversary, no equal, no end, no form, no limit; He does not dwell in anything, nor does any originated thing dwell in Him; movement and transference are not valid for Him; nor ignorance, lying, or deficiency; and that He will be seen in the hereafter, not in a place or direction; whatever He wills is, and whatever He does not will is not; He is not in need of anything, and nothing is obligatory upon Him; all actions of creatures are by His decree, power, will, and volition, but evil actions are not with His pleasure, command, and love.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of core Sunni beliefs about Allah. It begins with a poetic line expressing hope for sincerity, then lists the agreed-upon doctrines. First, the world is temporal (hadith) and the Maker eternal (qadim). The attributes are eternal (qadima), neither identical to the essence nor other than it — a key Ash'ari formulation. Then it negates anthropomorphism: no likeness, adversary, equal, end, form, limit. It negates indwelling (hulul) and originated events inhering in Him. It negates movement, ignorance, etc. It affirms the vision of Allah (ru'ya) in the afterlife without spatiality. It affirms absolute will and power: whatever He wills, is; whatever He does not will, is not. Nothing is obligatory upon Him. Finally, it affirmsthat all actions of creatures are by His decree and will, but evil actions are not with His pleasure, command, or love — a distinction to avoid attributing evil to Him in an approving sense.

Key Terms
رؤية
آخرة
مشيئة
إرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think seeing Allah implies He is in a place.
Correction: The text explicitly says not in a place or direction.

Checkpoint
Where will Allah be seen according to the passage?
A) In this world
B) In the afterlife, without spatiality
C) In a specific place called 'Arsh
D) Only in dreams

Key Takeaway
Allah will be seen by believers in Paradise, and His will is absolute and independent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you genuinely long to see Allah in the afterlife, or are your desires focused on worldly pleasures? What are you doing today to nurture that yearning?
?
If nothing happens outside Allah's will, then your past sins and present struggles were willed by Him. How does that truth change the way you view your mistakes and your need for His mercy?
?
Since Allah is not obligated to do anything for you, how does that shape your attitude in supplication? Do you rely on His mercy alone, or do you feel entitled to His answers?

Divine Decree and the Status of Evil Actions
Sanusi explains that all actions are decreed, but evil is not pleasing to Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that all actions are decreed by Allah, but evil deeds are not with His pleasure.

Core Idea
All actions occur by Allah's decree, but He does not approve of evil.

The final segment of this passage addresses the sensitive topic of predestination and moral evil. Sanusi affirms that all actions of creatures are by Allah's decree, power, will, and volition, but then qualifies that evil actions are not with His pleasure, command, or love.

Guided Path
1
Read the affirmation and qualification
Note 'كلُّ أعمال المخلوقات بقضائه وقدره وإرادته ومشيئته' and 'لكنَّ القبائح منها ليست برضَاهُ وأمرِهِ ومحبّتِهِ'.
2
Understand the comprehensive decree
All actions, good and evil, fall under Allah's decree and will.
3
Understand the distinction
Evil actions are not with Allah's approval or love, even though they occur by His will. This preserves divine justice.
4
Reflect on the importance
This prevents fatalism and avoids attributing evil to Allah directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هَذَا وَأَرْجُو اللَّهَ فِي الإِخْلَاصِ مِنَ الرِّياءِ ثُمَّ فِي الخَلَاصِ من (هذا) الذي ذكرتُه في هذه المنظومة من المتَّفق عليه بين أهل السُّنَّة العقائد: أنَّ العالم حادث، والصَّانع قديم، متّصف بصفات قديمة، ليست عينه ولا غيره، واحد لا شبيه له، ولا ضدَّ ولا نِدَّ ولا نهاية له، ولا صورة ولا حدَّ، ولا يَحُلُّ في شيء، ولا يقوم به حادث، ولا تصح عليه الحركة والانتقال، ولا الجهل ولا الكذب ولا النقص، وأنَّه يُرى فى الآخرة، وليس في حيّز وجهة، ما شاءَ كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن، ولا يحتاج إلى شيء، ولا يجب عليه شيءٌ، كلُّ أعمال المخلوقات بقضائه وقدره وإرادته ومشيئته، لكنَّ القبائح منها ليست برضَاهُ وأمرِهِ ومحبّتِهِ .
This – and I ask Allah for sincerity and freedom from hypocrisy, then for salvation – from what I have mentioned in this poem of the agreed-upon beliefs of Ahl al-Sunna: that the world is created, and the Maker is eternal, described with eternal attributes, which are neither His essence nor other than it, one with no likeness, no adversary, no equal, no end, no form, no limit; He does not dwell in anything, nor does any originated thing dwell in Him; movement and transference are not valid for Him; nor ignorance, lying, or deficiency; and that He will be seen in the hereafter, not in a place or direction; whatever He wills is, and whatever He does not will is not; He is not in need of anything, and nothing is obligatory upon Him; all actions of creatures are by His decree, power, will, and volition, but evil actions are not with His pleasure, command, and love.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of core Sunni beliefs about Allah. It begins with a poetic line expressing hope for sincerity, then lists the agreed-upon doctrines. First, the world is temporal (hadith) and the Maker eternal (qadim). The attributes are eternal (qadima), neither identical to the essence nor other than it — a key Ash'ari formulation. Then it negates anthropomorphism: no likeness, adversary, equal, end, form, limit. It negates indwelling (hulul) and originated events inhering in Him. It negates movement, ignorance, etc. It affirms the vision of Allah (ru'ya) in the afterlife without spatiality. It affirms absolute will and power: whatever He wills, is; whatever He does not will, is not. Nothing is obligatory upon Him. Finally, it affirmsthat all actions of creatures are by His decree and will, but evil actions are not with His pleasure, command, or love — a distinction to avoid attributing evil to Him in an approving sense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if Allah decrees evil, He must approve of it.
Correction: The passage distinguishes decree from approval: evil is decreed but not approved.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, are evil actions with Allah's pleasure?
A) Yes, because He decreed them
B) No, they are not with His pleasure, command, or love
C) Only some evil actions
D) The passage does not address this

Key Takeaway
All actions are decreed by Allah, but He does not approve of evil.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you ever blame Allah by saying 'it was decreed'? How does this lesson challenge that excuse? What one sin will you actively avoid this week, knowing that Allah permits it but never loves it?
?
Think of a serious evil you have witnessed or experienced. How does it comfort or challenge you to know that Allah did not approve of it, yet it still occurred by His will? Will you entrust the injustice to Him rather than despair?
?
If everything happens by Allah's will, is it possible to sincerely repent? How does the distinction between decree and approval give you the motivation to change? Write down one specific change you will make today because you know Allah loves goodness and hates evil.
